Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) ---
State Law reference— Municipalities generally, O.C.G.A. § 36-30-1 et seq.
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 2-1. - Election to use county registration list.
Authority. Pursuant to the authority granted in O.C.G.A. § 21-3-125, the city elects to use the registration system of
the county to maintain the registration list of electors of the city, and a copy thereof is available from the county
board of registrars.
Registration of electors. Any person who is a resident of the city and who is registered as an elector with the county
board of registrars and possesses the qualifications prescribed by the laws, and constitution of the state shall be
eligible to vote in a municipal primary or election in the city.
List of registered voters. At least 14 days prior to any election or primary held in the city a list of the registered
voters residing within the city shall be furnished to the city council.
(Ord. of 5-13-1985, §§ 1—3)
Sec. 2-2. - Recreation commission.
Established; composition; terms; vacancies. Under the provisions of House Bill 794, approved February 1, 1946, Act
No. 622 of the Georgia Municipal law, there is hereby established a recreation commission. This commission shall
be appointed by the city council and/or county commission and shall consist of not less than five or more than nine
persons serving without pay. The term of office shall be five years or until their successors are appointed and
qualified, except that the members of such a commission first appointed shall be appointed for such terms that the
term of one member shall expire annually thereafter. Vacancies in such commission occurring otherwise than by
expiration of term shall be filled by another appointment for the unexpired term.
Election of officers. Immediately after their appointment, they shall meet and organize by electing one of their
members president and such other officers as may be necessary. The recreation commission shall have power to
adopt bylaws, rules and regulations for the proper conduct of recreation for the city.
Duties and powers. The recreation commission shall provide, conduct and supervise public playground, playfields,
indoor recreation centers, and other recreation facilities owned or controlled by the city (town, village, or county). It
shall have the power to conduct any form of recreation or cultural activity that will employ the leisure time of the
people in a wholesome or constructive manner. It may conduct such activities on properties under its own control,
on public properties with the consent of the authorities thereof, and on private properties with the consent of the
owners.
Appointment of superintendent. The recreation commission shall have the power to appoint or designate someone
to act as superintendent who is trained or properly qualified for the work, and such other personnel as the
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
30/192
(e)
(f)
(a)
(b)
(a)
(b)
commission deems proper.
Budget. Annually the recreation commission shall submit a budget to the city council for its approval. The
commission may receive fees and revenues from the operation of recreation facilities and programs, and may also
solicit or receive any gifts or bequest of money or other personal property or any donations to be applied, principal
or income, for either temporary or permanent use for playgrounds or other recreation purposes.
Annual report. The recreation commission shall make an annual report to the city council and such other reports as
from time to time may be requested.
(Ord. of 2-19-1975, §§ 1—6)
Sec. 2-3. - Planning commission.
Composition; terms; vacancies; removal; compensation. The planning commission shall consist of five members,
who shall be residents of the city, appointed by the city council. The terms of the members shall be for four years,
except that in the appointment of the first planning commission. Under the terms of the ordinance from which this
section is derived, the first member shall be appointed for a term of one year, the second member shall be
appointed for a term of two years, the third members shall be appointed for a term of three years, and the
remaining members shall be appointed for a term of four years each. Any vacancy in membership shall be filled for
the unexpired term by the city council who shall also have the authority to remove any member for cause, on
written charges, after a public hearing. All members shall serve without compensation but may be reimbursed for
actual expenses incurred in connection with their official duties.
Powers and duties. From and after the time when the planning commission shall have organized and selected its
officers and shall have adopted its rules of procedure, then the planning commission shall have all the powers,
duties and responsibilities set forth in the state constitution.
(Ord. of 5-15-1989, §§ 1, 2)
Secs. 2-4—2-24. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - CITY COUNCIL
Sec. 2-25. - Meeting dates.
The council shall meet at least once per month. The regular meetings of the council shall be on the second Monday night of
each month, except in the month of January when the regular meeting shall be held on the first Monday night.
(Code 1973, § 2-1)
Sec. 2-26. - Compensation.
Mayor. The salary of the mayor is $200.00 per month.
Councilmembers. The compensation of members of the council is $75.00 per each regular meeting attended, and
$25.00 per each special meeting attended.
(Ord. of 9-4-2001, §§ I, II)
State law reference— Authority to fix compensation and benefits for officers and employees, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-4.
Secs. 2-27—2-55. - Reserved.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 2-56. - Oath and bond of ocers required.
Every officer, before entering upon the duties of his office, must take an oath similar to the oaths of the city councilmembers,
substituting his office for councilmember when the term "councilmember" occurs in said oath. Every officer appointed or elected
by the city council shall give such bond and security as is, or may be required of him, conditioned for the faithful performance of
his duty.
(Code 1973, § 2-3)
Sec. 2-57. - Grounds for removal or suspension of ocers.
An officer, elected by the city council, shall be removed from office or suspended as the council may elect for one or more of
the following causes:
Incompetence, misfeasance or malfeasance in office;
Conviction of a crime involving moral turpitude;
Abandonment of office or neglect to perform the duties thereof; or
Failure to perform the duties of office.
(Code 1973, § 2-4)
Secs. 2-58—2-87. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - CITY CLERK
Sec. 2-88. - Oath of oce.
Before entering upon the duties of his office, the city clerk shall take the following oath: "I do solemnly swear (or affirm) that I
will well and truly demean myself as City Clerk of the City of Edison, and I will keep a true record of the proceedings of said City
Council, and perform such other duties as may be required of me as Clerk. Further, I will properly demean myself as Treasurer of
the City of Edison, that I will keep a true record of the finances of the City and keep a true account of monies expended and
received by said corporation, and well and truly account of all monies expended and received by said corporation, and well and
truly account for same, so help me God."
(Code 1973, § 2-27)
Sec. 2-89. - Duties; general enumeration.
The general duties of the city clerk are to:
Keep correct and full minutes of the proceedings of the city council together with all ordinances and
resolutions passed by it, in a book or register kept for that purpose.
Receive all applications or petitions made to the city, to place them before the mayor, or city councilmember,
at the meeting of the council next succeeding the receipt thereof.
Attend all council meetings.
Receive all applications for licenses and to issue the same as prescribed by ordinance.

money, and his book shall at all times be subject to examination by the council.
Pay out no money except upon orders passed by the city council, drawn up and signed by him, and
countersigned by the mayor, or in his absence, by the mayor pro tem.
Correct all executions for taxes or fines.
(Code 1973, §§ 2-29, 2-30)

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 2-107. - Fees and charges.
Whenever in this Code or in any ordinance it is provided that any fee or charge is "as established by the city" or substantially
similar language appears, such language shall mean that the fee is as provided by ordinance. Such fees may be consolidated into a
fee schedule.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
33/192
Sec. 2-108. - Payment of claims after council approval.
All claims against the city, other than for officials' salaries and expenses, shall be left with the city clerk at least two days before
any regular meeting of the city council. If the council approves the payment of the same, then the city clerk shall draw an order for
the same on the treasurer.
(Code 1973, § 2-31)

FOOTNOTE(S):

State Law reference— Budgets and audits, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-1 et seq.
Sec. 2-130. - Fiscal year.
The fiscal year of the city shall begin on July 1 of each year and end on the following June 30th.
(Ord. of 7-1-1979)
State law reference— Establishment of fiscal year, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-3.
Sec. 2-131. - Annual budget.
An annual budget for the city and for each department thereof shall be adopted on or before the last meeting in June of each
year for the ensuing fiscal year.
(Ord. of 7-1-1979, § 17-2)
State law reference— Adoption of budget, O.C.G.A. § 36-3-6.
Sec. 2-132. - Quarterly reports.
There shall be prepared and issued at the end of each quarter during the fiscal year a budget report on the accounting system
and placed on file in the minutes of the city council.
(Ord. of 7-1-1979, § 17-4)
Sec. 2-133. - Accounting method established.
There shall be established and maintained a double entry accounting system on a cash basis and all accounts shall be posted
promptly.
(Ord. of 7-1-1979, § 17-5)

State Law reference— Preferences for products manufactured in state, O.C.G.A. § 36-84-1 et seq.; Georgia Local Government
Public Works Construction Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-91-1 et seq.
Sec. 2-165. - Signed requisition and recordkeeping required.
The mayor or mayor pro tem is the agent for the city for the purpose of purchasing all goods, wares, fixtures or supplies of any
kind for the city and all purchases made shall be made through the mayor's or mayor pro tem's office by requisition upon the city
clerk, which requisition shall be signed by the particular department head and by the city clerk, or mayor. The city clerk is required
to keep a copy of all purchase orders and all requisitions on file in his office. No purchase order is required for any purchase of
$100.00 or less.
(Code 1973, § 2-5)
Sec. 2-166. - Sealed bids required for items costing more than $5,000.00.
No purchases of any kind whatsoever exceeding the cost of $5,000.00 shall be made by the city without first obtaining sealed
bids on such purchases by the city from not less than two separate and distinct suppliers or sellers. Said purchase shall be made
from the lowest bid received; exception may be made in cases of emergency or necessity, such cases to be adjudged by the
council.
(Code 1973, § 2-6)
Chapter 4 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) ---
State Law reference— Alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq.; local regulation of alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-1 et seq.
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 4-1. - Denitions.
The definitions in O.C.G.A. § 3-1-2 apply to this chapter.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 1)
Sec. 4-2. - Malt beverages tax.
Imposed. There is hereby imposed upon all wholesale dealers selling malt beverages within the city a specific excise
tax as follows:
Where malt beverages, commonly known as tap or draft beer, are sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, a
tax of $6.00 on each container sold containing not more than 15½ gallons and a proportionate tax at the same
rate on all fractional parts of 15½ gallons.
Where malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans, or other containers, except barrel or bulk containers, a tax of
$0.05 per 12 ounces and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 12 ounces.
Tax in addition to other charges. The excise tax provided for in subsection (a) of this section shall be in addition to
any license fee, tax or charge which may now or in the future be imposed upon the business of selling malt

Penalty. The failure to make a timely report and remittance shall render a wholesale dealer liable for a penalty equal
to five percent of the total amount due during the first 30-day period following the date such report and remittance
were due and a further penalty of five percent of the amount of such remittance for each successive 30-day period,
or any portion thereof, during which such report and remittance are not filed. The filing of a false or fraudulent
report shall render the wholesale dealer making such report liable for a penalty equal to 50 percent of the amount
of the remittance which would be required under an accurate and truthful report.
(Code 1973, §§ 3-24, 3-27, 3-28)
State law reference— Tax on malt beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-80 et seq.
Sec. 4-3. - Wine tax.
In addition to the annual retail license fee required, there is hereby levied an excise tax on the first sale or use of wine by the
package computed at the rate of $0.22 per liter and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter sold,
displayed or stored in the city. Said tax shall be paid to the city by the wholesale distributor on all wines sold to retailers in the city,
as follows: Each wholesale distributor selling, shipping, or in any way delivering wine to any retailer, shall collect the excise tax at
the time of delivery and shall remit the same together with a summary of all deliveries to each retailer on or before the 20th day of
the month following. It shall be unlawful and a violation of the ordinance from which this section is derived for any wholesale
distributor to sell, ship or delivery in any manner any wine to a retailer without having collected said tax. It shall be unlawful and a
violation of this section for any retailer to possess, own, hold, store, display or sell any wine on which such tax has not been paid.
Each wholesaler shall be paid three percent of the amount of taxes collected as reimbursement of collection of said tax. Every wine
distributor shall deliver a copy of each delivery ticket to the city clerk after making a delivery, said delivery ticket to show the exact
quantity delivered and the amount of tax collected thereon
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 15; Ord. of 2-13-1984)
State law reference— Wine tax, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-60.
Sec. 4-4. - Persons eligible for licenses; nancial responsibility required.
No license required by the provisions of this chapter shall be issued to:
Any applicant who is not of good moral character. Corporation applicants shall be of good business reputation.
An applicant who has been convicted under any federal, state, local law or ordinance of a criminal offense
involving moral turpitude, or has been convicted under any federal, state or local law of any criminal offense
involving alcoholic beverages, gambling, or tax law violations, if such conviction tends to indicate that the
applicant would not maintain the operation for which he is seeking a license in conformity with law or
ordinance.
A person whose place of business is conducted by an employee, manager or agent unless the manager, agent
or employee possesses the same qualifications as the licensee. Corporation applicants shall be of good
business reputation.
A person who does not possess financial responsibility. Financial statements must be submitted with each
completed application as prescribed by the council. Evidence of financial responsibility shall include evidence
that the person can obtain adequate liability insurance for the business and premises to be licensed.
No license shall be issued for any location or premises where the sale of any alcoholic beverages to be sold under
the license is prohibited by state law or city ordinance.
No license shall be granted to any person who is not at least 21 years of age unless the business is managed by a
person who is at least 21 years of age.

Sec. 4-5. - Toilet facility only to be accessible from inside building.
All toilets or restroom facilities maintained in the premises of any business engaged in the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be
entered only from the inside of the building in which any such business is conducted, and shall not be accessible from the outside.
(Code 1973, § 3-1)

ARTICLE II. - MALT BEVERAGES AND WINE PACKAGE STORES
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) ---
State Law reference— Malt beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-1 et seq.; wine, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-1 et seq.
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 4-31. - Penalties.
Any person violating this article shall be punished as provided in general penalty section 1-7, and such conviction shall
automatically revoke the permit and license of the one so convicted.
(Code 1973, § 3-34)
Sec. 4-32. - Right of entry.
The mayor or city police shall have the right to enter upon the premises where malt beverages or wine is sold at retail in the
city, at any reasonable hour when such business is open, for the purpose of checking on the amount of malt beverages or wine on
hand and to make such other reasonable investigation of such retail sales of malt beverages or wine as will furnish information on
the number of sales of such retail malt beverages or wine dealer.
(Code 1973, § 3-29)
Sec. 4-33. - Signs warning no liquor drinking on premises required.
Every person engaged in the sale of malt beverages or wine shall display prominently in such place of business a sign in bold
letters: "DRINKING OF WHISKEY OR ANY SPIRITUOUS LIQUOR PROHIBITED ON THESE PREMISES."
(Code 1973, § 3-2)
Sec. 4-34. - Wholesaling to unlicensed retailers prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any wholesale dealer in malt beverages or wine to sell, dispense or deliver any malt beverages or wine
to any person who is not duly authorized and licensed to sell malt beverages or wine at retail within the city.

Sec. 4-35. - Closing hours.
Enumerated. Any business selling malt beverages or wine in the city shall close said place of business not later than
12:00 midnight on each day said business is open for operation, and remain closed until 7:00 a.m. following.
Revocation of license for violation. Should any person keeping any business wherein is sold or offered for sale malt
beverages or wine, sell or offer the same for sale after 12:00 midnight and before 7:00 a.m. on any day, or otherwise
violate this chapter or applicable state law, the license to sell beer or wine shall be revoked by the city, and no new
license for such sales shall be issued or allowed to such person for the sale of malt beverages or wine in such
business location for a period of one year from the date of said revocation; and no license for such sales of malt
beverages or wine shall be issued to the person holding such revoked license, or to who such license which was
revoked had previously been issued for a period of one year from the date of such revocation.
(Code 1973, §§ 3-5, 3-6)

DIVISION 2. - LICENSE
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (3) ---
State Law reference— Local malt beverage licenses, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-40 et seq.; local wine licenses, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-40.
Sec. 4-56. - Required.
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell any malt beverages or wine within the limits of the city without first obtaining from
the council a license to sell the same.
(Code 1973, § 3-30)
Sec. 4-57. - Application required; investigation and report; action by council.
Persons desiring to sell malt beverages or wine shall file a license application with the city clerk, who shall refer the
same to the chief of police or mayor or his designee for investigation. Said officer shall investigate:
The moral fitness and reputation of the applicant;
The applicant's reputation as a peaceful citizen or law violator;
The general character and reputation of the applicant's place of business; and
Any other facts that the council should know in considering the granting of a permit and license to the
applicant.
It shall be the duty of said officer to report his findings to the council at the next regular meeting or as soon
thereafter as possible, at which the applicant shall personally appear, which body shall either grant or refuse the
permit and license.
(Code 1973, § 3-31)
Sec. 4-58. - Conditions required for lawful establishment.

ARTICLE III. - MALT BEVERAGE AND WINE SALES FOR ON-PREMISES CONSUMPTION
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (4) ---
State Law reference— Malt beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-1 et seq.; wine, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-1 et seq.
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 4-75. - Denitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section,
except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
Church means a regular house of worship.
Conviction means an adjudication of guilt or a plea of guilty, or a plea of nolo contendere or the forfeiture of bond by a person
charged with a crime.
Distance means the measurement in a straight line in linear feet from the nearest wall enclosing the proposed premises of the
licensee to the nearest property line of any school, college or church.
Licensee means the authorization by the city council to engage in the sale of malt beverages for on-premises consumption.
Premises means the definite closed area wherein malt beverages are sold, which is owned by or under control of the person to
whom the license is issued.
Retail sale means the selling or offering for sale any malt beverage or wine to any member of the public.
School or college means only such state, county, city, church or other schools as teach subjects commonly taught in the
common schools of this state.

Sec. 4-93. - Required.
Term; prohibited acts. No person shall sell malt beverages or wine for on-premises consumption without first
obtaining a city license for the calendar year in which such business in the city is conducted. No person shall sell
malt beverages for on-premises consumption after such license has expired or been revoked.
Class of license. This license shall be for the sale of malt beverages or wine for on-premises consumption. No malt
beverage shall be sold at retail for consumption on the premises except at a:
Restaurant, described as any public place kept, used, maintained, advertised and held out to the public as a
place where meals are served and where meals are actually regularly served, such place being provided with
adequate and sanitary kitchen and dining room equipment and having employed there in sufficient number
and kind of employees to prepare, cook and serve suitable food for its guest.
Tavern, which means a place of entertainment for the accommodation of the public where malt beverages or
wine is sold at retail for on-premises consumption.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, §§ 3A-2, 3A-18)

Required; contents. The application for license shall be in writing and addressed to the council, and shall set forth
therein the following information:
The location of the place of business wherein malt beverages or wine are to be sold;
The age, name and present occupation of applicant; and
The names and ages of persons who shall be employed in the carrying on of such business.
The application shall be signed by the applicant and must be verified by oath of such applicant. Such application and
oath must be on a form provided by the city clerk.
Fee. All applicants for license shall pay a fee in an amount as established from time to time by the city at the time

Sec. 4-95. - Notice of application.
All applicants for a license shall, within ten days after filing of such application, publish an advertisement in the
official newspaper of the city wherein all legal advertisements are published to the effect that such application has
been made, listing the name of the applicant, the complete address of the place of business where such application
for the sale of malt beverages is proposed, and the date of the hearing thereon. This advertisement shall run for a
period of two weeks preceding the next regular meeting of the council. Such advertisement shall be filed with the
proper officer or agent of such paper within ten days following the date of application. The cost of such
advertisement shall be paid by the applicant and a copy of the published notice shall be filed with the city clerk.
The advertisement required by subsection (a) of this section shall be and read substantially as follows:
Notice of Application for Retail License to sell malt beverages or wine. The undersigned has made application to the
Council of Edison, Georgia for a retail license to sell malt beverages or wine for on premises consumption at ____________.
This application will be heard by the Council at its regular meeting to be held at ____________ o'clock p.m. on the
____________ day of ____________, ____________.
No application for a license under this division shall be acted upon or issued by the council until after advertisement
and public hearing thereon, as required therein.
A public hearing upon all applications for a license under this division shall be held before the council at its regular
meeting not less than 30 days or more than 60 days after the filing of the application.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, § 3A-4)
Sec. 4-96. - Police investigation and report required.
All applicants shall be investigated by the police department or such other person as may be designated by the council. The
report of such investigation shall be presented to the council for consideration with the application.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, § 3A-5)

Sec. 4-97. - Fingerprints.
Each applicant for a license to sell malt beverages or wine in this division who has not heretofore been licensed by
the city to sell alcoholic beverages, at retail, shall be required to submit to a complete fingerprinting record and test,
pursuant to the rules and regulations established by the city from time to time, the same being used by the city to
supplement the information contained on the application and to make available to the city any records of criminal
offenses, either federal or state from other jurisdictions.
The council, within its own discretion, from time to time may require employees, male and female, working in any
establishment dispensing malt beverages or wine, to submit to the same complete fingerprinting record and test
and for the same purposes of supplementing any information available to the city with respect to employees.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, § 3A-7)
Sec. 4-98. - Distance requirements; reissue after denial or revocation.
It shall be unlawful to issue any license under this article within 300 feet of any church.
It shall be unlawful to issue any license under this article within 300 feet of the grounds of any school or school
building.
In the event the council revokes or denies any license at any location within the city, no new license shall be granted
by the city for the period of six months after the date of revocation or denial, at the same location. After notice to
the council that a person holding a license or his employee or agent, has been accused of prohibited acts, no new
license shall be issued for such location until after the disposition of the complaint.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, § 3A-8)
Sec. 4-99. - Duration; renewals.
All licenses granted pursuant to this article shall expire on December 31 of the year in which the same shall be
issued. The fee shall be due and payable in advance by January 1 of each year.
Licensees who desire to renew their license shall file applications with the requisite fees heretofore provided with
the city clerk on the form provided for renewal of the license for the ensuing year. Applications for renewal must be
filed December 1 of each year, otherwise no renewal license shall be granted; but an application for renewal shall be
required and shall be treated as an initial application, and the applicant shall be required to comply with all rules
and regulations for the granting of licenses as if no previous license has been held. All licenses granted hereunder
shall be for the calendar year and the full license fee must be paid for a license issued at any time during the license
year.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, §§ 3A-11, 3A-21)
Sec. 4-100. - Nontransferable.
Licenses issued under authority of this article shall not be transferable from one person to another nor from one location to
another except with the express written approval of the council.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, § 3A-9)
Sec. 4-101. - Suspension; revocation.
Any license which has been issued or which may hereafter be issued by the city to any licensee may be suspended
or revoked for the due cause as hereinafter defined, and after a hearing held for the purpose of considering any
such suspension or revocation. At least five days prior written notice of a time, place and purpose of such hearing, a
statement of the charge or charges upon which such hearing shall be held shall be given to the holder of such
license which is sought to be suspended or revoked.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
42/192
(b)
(c)
(d)
Due cause for the suspension or revocation of any license shall consist of a violation of any laws or ordinances regulati
business, or violation of regulations made pursuant to authority granted for the purpose of regulating such business, o
violation of any state, federal, municipal ordinance that would prevent one from obtaining a license, or for violation of
provision of this chapter.
The mayor is hereby authorized to suspend any license issued under this article in any emergency situation such as
civil disorders or natural disasters or in any situation that he deems some immediate suspension necessary for the
protection of the health and welfare of the citizens of the city, and the suspension may be effective immediately and
shall remain in force until the mayor determines the emergency is over or until the next regular meeting of the
council.
When a license is suspended or revoked, the city shall not be required to refund any portion of the license fee to the
holder of such suspended or revoked license. When a license is revoked, the licensee may not reapply for a license
under this article for a period of three years from such revocation.
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, § 3A-13)
Sec. 4-102. - Sales under suspended license prohibited.
No person whose license has been suspended or revoked pursuant to any provisions of this chapter shall sell any beverages
covered by the suspended or revoked license during the period of such suspension or after revocation. No license shall be
suspended or revoked without the council first giving to said licensee written notice of the reason thereof, and within five days
thereafter the licensee shall have the right of a hearing before the council and may present any evidence or give any reason why
the license should not be suspended or revoked, except for the suspension provided for in section 4-101(c).
(Ord. of 7-17-2001, § 3A-14)

ARTICLE IV. - PACKAGE SALES OF DISTILLED SPIRITS
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (6) ---
State Law reference— Distilled spirits, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-1 et seq.
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 4-133. - Copy of article to be kept on licensed premises; licensee responsible for acts of employees.
All holders of a license for the sale of distilled spirits shall keep a copy of the ordinance from which this article is derived in his
premises and shall instruct any person working there with respect to the terms of this article and each licensee or his agents
selling distilled spirits shall at all times be familiar with the terms of this article. The licensee shall be held responsible for any acts
of his employees in any violation of this article or of the laws of the state or the rules and regulations of the state revenue
commissioner.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 20)
Sec. 4-134. - Authority to inspect.
The business premises of the holder of a retail distilled spirits license for the sale of distilled spirits shall be open to inspection
at any and all times by officers or officials authorized to conduct such inspections.

(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 21)
Sec. 4-135. - Package sales only.
All retailers licensed under this article shall sell or offer to sell in the original unbroken package only and shall sell no package
containing less than one-half pint.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 7)
State law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-26.
Sec. 4-136. - Tax.
In addition to the annual retail distilled spirits license fee, there is hereby levied an excise tax computed at the rate of $0.22
per liter of distilled spirits, excluding fortified wine, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter which
shall be paid to the city on all distilled spirits sold, displayed or stored in said city. Said tax shall be due and payable to the city by
the wholesale distributor on all distilled spirits sold to retailers in the city at the time of delivery and remitted the together with a
summary of all deliveries to each retailer on or before the 20th day of the month following. It shall be unlawful and a violation of
this article for any wholesale distributor to sell, ship or delivery in any manner any distilled spirits to a retailer without having
collected said tax. It shall be unlawful and a violation of this article for any retailer to possess, own, hold, store, display or sell any
distilled spirits on which such tax has not been paid. Each wholesaler shall be paid three percent of the amount of taxes collected
as reimbursement of collection of said tax. Every distilled spirits distributor shall deliver a copy of each delivery ticket to the city
clerk after making a delivery, said delivery ticket to show the exact quantity delivered and the amount of tax collected thereon
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 15; Ord. of 2-13-1984)
State law reference— Local tax authorized, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-80.
Sec. 4-137. - Sales and deliveries to take place on business premises.
No retailer shall sell or deliver any distilled spirits to any person except in said retailer's place of business.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 9)
Sec. 4-138. - Sale of other products.
No retailer shall sell or offer for sale or display or keep in stock, at his place of business where distilled spirits are
offered for sale, any other product or commodity, except the following:
Wines, when properly licensed;
Beverages containing no alcohol commonly used to dilute distilled spirits;
Malt beverages or beer, when properly licensed;
Tobacco products; and
Packaged ice.
No beverages or packages of ice may be opened or consumed in said place of business.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 8)
Sec. 4-139. - Days and hours of sale.
No retailer shall be in his place of business or open his place of business, or furnish, sell or offer for sale any distilled spirits or
other alcoholic beverages, with the exemptions set forth in this article, at any of the following times:
At any time Thanksgiving Day or Christmas Day;

At any time in violation of a local ordinance or regulation or of a special order of the council; or
On any day before 8:00 a.m. or after 11:45 p.m.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 10; Ord. of 8-11-1986)
State law reference— Hours of sale of alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-20.
Sec. 4-140. - Storage.
No licensed retailer shall keep any distilled spirits stored in any bonded or other type warehouse in the city, nor shall he enter
into any type of arrangement whereby distilled spirits ordered by him is stored for him by any licensed wholesaler. A retailer shall
keep no inventory or stock of distilled spirits at any place except his licensed place of business, and within his licensed place of
business his storage space for distilled spirits shall be immediately adjacent to the room in which he is licensed to do business.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 13)
Sec. 4-141. - Gambling prohibited; exceptions.
Except as authorized by law, there shall be no gambling, betting, games of chance, punchboards, vending machines, slot
machines, pin ball machines, pool tables, lotteries or tickets or chances therein or the operation of any schemes for hazarding
money or any other thing of value in any licensed retailer's place of business or in any room adjoining the same, owned, leased or
controlled by licensee and any violation of this section shall be cause for suspension or revocation of license.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 24)
Secs. 4-142—4-165. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE
Sec. 4-166. - Required.
A separate retail distilled spirits license shall be required for each place of business.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 5)
Sec. 4-167. - Application and license term and renewal.
An application for a retail distilled spirits license shall be made, on forms furnished by the city.
A retail distilled spirits license shall be valid only for the calendar year indicated thereon and no such licenses may
be renewed. A licensee who desires to continue in business during the next or subsequent calendar year must make
a new application for such year on or before November 1 of the preceding year.
In addition to the completion and submission of application form as required by the city, each applicant shall attach
thereto a completed application form with all attachments and requirements for a state license.
Before any retail distilled spirits license is granted, the applicant must post with the city, along with his application, a
personal performance bond; said bond to be conditioned requiring the faithful observance and performance by the
licensee of the rules and regulations contained in the ordinance from which this division is derived. Upon a violation
of this article or any part thereof, the amount of the bond to be forfeited will be determined by the seriousness of
the violations as determined by the council after a hearing is held by the council after a three day written notice is
given the violator. Said bond is to be payable to the city in the amount of $500.00, said bond to be approved by the
council and shall be executed in a form to be furnished.

All applications for a retail distilled spirits license shall be presented in person.
The making of any statement on an application for a license to sell liquor distilled spirits which shall be later found
to be false shall constitute grounds for revocation of said license.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, §§ 14, 18, 22)
Sec. 4-168. - Maximum number of licenses issued to one person.
Only two retail distilled spirits licenses shall be issued to any one person in the city, and no person who holds a retail distilled
spirits license in any other county or municipality of the state, shall be eligible to receive a retail distilled spirits license. As used in
this section, the term "person" includes all members of such licensee's family and the term "family" includes any person related to
the holder of such license within the first degree of consanguinity or affinity as computed according to the civil law.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 3)
Sec. 4-169. - Restrictions—Location.
Each application for a retail distilled spirits license shall include a scale drawing of the location of the proposed premises
showing the distance to the nearest church or school or a certificate of a registered surveyor that such location complies with
O.C.G.A. § 3-3-21.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 4)
Sec. 4-170. - Same—Building.
No retail distilled spirits license shall be issued to any person unless the building in which the business will be located is
complete and detailed plans of said building and outside premises are attached to the application, or unless the a building permit
and plans and specifications of a proposed building to be built are attached to the application. The completed building or the
proposed building shall comply with ordinances of the city, regulations of the state revenue commissioner and the laws of the
state. The proposed building shall also be subject to final inspection and approval when completed by the building inspector. Each
building in which the business will be located shall contain sufficient lighting so that the building itself and the premise on all sides
of the building are readily visible at all times from the front of the street on which the building is located so as to reveal the inside
retail area of the building and so as to reveal all of the outside premises of said building. Each applicant for a retail distilled spirits
license shall attach to his application evidence of ownership of the building or proposed building or a copy of the lease if the
applicant is leasing the building.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 6)
Sec. 4-171. - Fee.
The annual fee for a retail distilled spirits license shall be paid prior to the issuance of any license, said fee to accompany the
application and shall be either in cash or a bank certified check. Such fee shall be in an amount as established from time to time by
the city.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 15; Ord. of 2-13-1984)
Sec. 4-172. - Nontransferable and nonassignable.
No retail distilled spirits license shall be transferable or assignable to any person or other location, and in the event that a
licensed business is sold or closed, it shall be the duty of the licensee to immediately surrender his license to the city.

Sec. 4-173. - Display.
Licenses under this article shall be displayed prominently at all times on the premises for which same was issued.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 25)
Sec. 4-174. - Revocation or suspension.
In addition to any penalty contained in section 1-7 or otherwise:
A violation of this article by a licensee is grounds for the revocation of a license issued under this article.
A violation of state or federal laws and regulations of the state revenue commissioner relating to the sale and
distribution of distilled spirits by a licensee shall subject the licensee to the immediate suspension or
revocation of his license.
(Ord. of 2-14-1977, § 26)
Chapter 6 - ANIMALS
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) ---
State Law reference— Animals, O.C.G.A. § 4-1-1 et seq.; cruelty to animals, O.C.G.A. § 16-12-4.
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 6-1. - Denitions.
For the purposes of this chapter the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the meaning indicated in
this section unless the context requires otherwise.
Abused animal means any animal which is:
Mistreated, beaten, tormented or teased;
Deprived of water, food or shelter;
Kept under unsanitary conditions;
Abandoned; or
Trained for fighting other animals.
Animal means a multicellular organism of the kingdom Animalia, differing from plants in certain typical characteristics such as
a capacity for locomotion, nonphotosynthetic metabolism pronounced response to stimuli, restricted growth, and fixed bodily
structure.
Animal control board means a board consisting of the mayor and two other city councilmembers appointed by the city council.
Animal control officer means the person charged by the city council with enforcing this chapter.
At heel means a condition in which an animal is in the immediate vicinity of its owner and clearly under the voice control of
that person and that control is clearly being exerted.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
47/192
(1)
(2)
a.
b.
c.
At large means an animal shall be deemed at large when the animal is in any public street right-of-way, park or other public
grounds, or when off the said premises of the owner or person who has custody of said animal, and not under restraint or under
the immediate control (at heel) of the owner or the person who has custody of said animal.
Cat means a feline of whatever breed and all ages.
Court means the municipal court of the city with jurisdiction to hear violations of city ordinances.
Owner means any natural person or any legal entity, including, but not limited to, a corporation, partnership, firm, or trust
owning, possessing, harboring, keeping, or having custody or control of an animal within this city.
Poison means a substance that through its chemical action usually kills, injures or impairs an organism.
Potentially dangerous dogs.
The term "potentionally dangerous dogs" means any dog that bites a human being without provocation on
either public or private property at any time after January 1, 1999.
The term "potentionally dangerous dogs" does not include:
Dogs which merely chase someone or act aggressively;
Dogs used by law enforcement officers; or
Dogs who attack in response to torment, abuse, or assault.
Pound means those premises designated by the city council for the purpose of holding and caring for animals found to be at
large by those persons charged with the enforcement of these regulations.
Proper enclosure means an enclosure for keeping a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog while on the owners
property, securely enclosed indoors or in a securely enclosed and locked pen, fence, or structure suitable to prevent the entry of
young children and designed to prevent the dog from escaping. Any such pen or structure shall have secure sides and a secure
top, and, if the dog is enclosed with a fence, all sides of the fence shall be of sufficient height and the bottom of the fence
constructed or secured in such a manner as to prevent the dog's escape either from over or from under the fence. Any such
enclosure shall also provide protection from the elements for the dog.
Rabies vaccination means the inoculation of an animal with an approved rabies vaccine.
Severe injury means any physical injury that results in broken bones or disfiguring lacerations requiring multiple sutures or
cosmetic surgery or a physical injury that results in death.
Under restraint means secured by a leash or lead not to exceed six feet in length held by a responsible, able bodied person.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, §§ 1.01, 1.02)
Sec. 6-2. - Interference with ocials prohibited.
No person shall resist or interfere with an animal control officer or any other city official in the performance of his official duty
in enforcing this chapter, nor shall any person fail or refuse to exhibit the vaccination certificate of any animal required to be
vaccinated by this chapter when required to do so by any animal control officer or other city official.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.03)
Sec. 6-3. - Hogs prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep within the city any hog.
(Code 1973, § 4-1)
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
48/192
Sec. 6-4. - Nuisance animals.
The council, upon formal complaint by any citizen concerning an animal, shall conduct an investigation to determine whether
the animal constitutes a nuisance. If the council determines that the animal does constitute a nuisance, the owner of the animal
shall be so notified and shall be given a reasonable period of time during which to correct those conditions constituting the
nuisance. Failure to correct said nuisance within a period of time considered reasonable by the council shall be punishable as
prescribed in general penalty section 1-7.
(Code 1973, § 4-17)
Sec. 6-5. - Abandonment prohibited.
No person shall release an animal on any property public or private, with the intention of abandoning the animal.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.09)
Sec. 6-6. - Livestock on public rights-of-way prohibited.
No one shall allow or permit any horses, cattle, sheep, goats, or other livestock to run at large on public rights-of-way or to be
staked so that they can go upon public rights-of-way or to drive or lead any such animals along or on the public rights-of-way
unless fastened to a rope, chain or other substantial leading device, which rope, chain or other substantial leading device is
securely held by a responsible person during all the time that such animals are being led or driven along and over the public rightsof-way.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.08)
Sec. 6-7. - Unlawful to permit animals in heat to roam or run free.
No owner or custodian of any animal in heat shall permit the animal to roam free. Such animal shall be confined in a building
or securely enclosed in a manner that shall not allow contact with a non-neutered male animal except for planned breeding.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.11)
Secs. 6-8—6-32. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - DEAD ANIMALS UPON PUBLIC OR PRIVATE PROPERTY
Sec. 6-33. - Prohibited; exception.
No person shall abandon a dead animal on any public property or public right-of-way unless the place in which the animal is
being left is a public dump or other facility designed for receiving such and had been designated by the city as a public facility for
receiving trash or refuse.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.05)
Sec. 6-34. - Removal from public rights-of-way.
The owner of dead animals upon the public rights-of-way, shall remove the same so as not to constitute a nuisance. If the
owner fails to do so the city shall remove and dispose of such carcass on public rights-of-way, and charge the cost of such removal
and disposal to the owner of the carcass if known.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.04)
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
49/192
Sec. 6-35. - Removal from private property.
When any animal is found on private property, the owner of the dead animal or the owner of the premises upon which such
animal is located shall remove the same immediately at his own cost. Failure to do so in a timely manner is hereby declared a
nuisance and constitutes a violation of this chapter.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.06)
Sec. 6-36. - Abandonment upon private property.
No person shall intentionally abandon a dead animal on any private property belonging to another unless the person so doing
shall have first obtained permission from the owner of the property on which the animal is being left.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 2.07)
Secs. 6-37—6-60. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 6-61. - Animal control department designated.
The authority and responsibility for administration of these regulations shall rest with the city council. In exercising that
authority and discharging that responsibility the council shall designate the animal control department head to be charged with
enforcing this chapter. The animal control department shall coordinate and cooperate with the county health department and such
other agencies as the council deems advisable. The animal control department head shall issue interpretations on this chapter
upon written request.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 8.03)
Sec. 6-62. - Duty of animal control ocer.
It shall be the duty of the animal control officer under the direction of the animal control department head to enforce these
regulations.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 8.04)
Sec. 6-63. - Authority to kill certain animals.
Any animal found at large in violation of this chapter, which cannot be safely impounded or poses a real threat to city officials
citizens, other domesticated animals or livestock may be slain by any police officer, or animal control officer when in the presence
of and having had permission given by a police officer. Such measures shall only be used when tranquilizing the animal fails or
there is a significant risk of immediate danger.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 6.03)
Secs. 6-64—6-84. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - IMPOUNDMENT

Sec. 6-85. - Conscation of suspected abused animals.
If an animal control officer or any law enforcement officer has reasonable cause to believe that any animal is subject to abuse,
he shall confiscate and impound the animal pending the conclusion of an investigation. Said investigation shall he completed by
the end of the seventh business day, at which time a finding shall he issued by the animal control officer and the department head
of the city animal control. If a finding is made that the animal is being abused, cruelty to animal charges shall be filed against the
owner and the animal will become the property of the city. In the event that a determination is reached that the animal is not being
abused, the animal will be returned to the owner, and followup investigations may be conducted by the animal control officer at
the discretion of the department head of the city animal control and the animal control officer. The responsibility for costs related
to the confiscation and impoundment during the investigation will rest with the owner regardless of the determination reached.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 6.02)
Sec. 6-86. - Procedure when animal running at large.
It shall be the duty of the animal control officer to apprehend any animal found running at large contrary to the
provisions of this chapter and impound such animal in the animal shelter designated by the city council.
All animals impounded by the city shall be held until claimed by the owner for a minimum of two calendar days to
include the day the animal was impounded, whichever comes first. Longer periods of custody may be used if in the
opinion of the holding agency personnel the animal is likely to be claimed by its owner or a new owner will be
found, provided that in either case there is a reasonable expectation that the fees, fines, or other charges provided
for in this division will be paid.
Any animal not claimed within the times provided in subsection (b) of this section shall become the property of the
agency serving as the city's animal shelter to dispose of humanely in accordance with their regulations and policies.
In lieu of, apprehending and impounding an animal found at large, the animal control officer, upon determining the
owner, may return the animal to the owner (if able to apprehend said animal) and issue a summons requiring the
owner to appear in the court of jurisdiction for violation of this chapter. Said summons may be issued without
apprehending the animal if the owner of said animal can be identified.
It shall be the responsibility of the animal control officer to make reasonable efforts to ascertain the owner of each
impounded animal as soon as possible after taking it into custody. If the owner is identified, a reasonably
expeditious effort shall be made to notify said owner of the impoundment of the animal and make the owner aware
of the city animal control laws, the period of impounding, charges to be made and any fees owed the city.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 4.01)
Sec. 6-87. - Reclamation.
Any person may make application to the agency designated by the city council to operate a pound for the city for
the return of any animal impounded therein and upon presentation of proof satisfactory to the agency that such
person is rightly entitled to the possession of such animal may recover it upon presentation of an impound fee to be
fixed by agreement between the city council and said agency, together with the reasonable expense of the animal's
keep. The agency shall retain any fees collected by it under this section.
No animal shall be released to a potential new owner prior to the end of the impoundment period stipulated in
section 6-86(b).
If after consultation with a licensed veterinarian, an animal is determined to have a terminal illness, a potentially
lethal wound or (in the case of an animal whose owner has not been identified) a communicable disease, such
animal shall be disposed of by humane methods without regard to the specified holding period.
Enforcement personnel following the procedures proscribed in this chapter shall not be held liable for the disposal
of any animal.

Sec. 6-88. - Proof of rabies vaccination required prior to release.
No animal required to be vaccinated for rabies shall be released from impoundment prior to showing proof of a current rabies
inoculation. If said animal has not had a current rabies vaccine or it cannot be shown that it has a current rabies vaccine the animal
shall be vaccinated prior to being released. The owner of the animal shall be responsible for the costs of the vaccination.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 4.03)
Sec. 6-89. - Physical facilities required.
The city animal shelter shall be located at a place or agency designated by the city council.
The facilities shall be constructed so as to provide security for the citizens of the surrounding area and for the
animals under impoundment.
Facilities for sanitary storage of feed and secure storage of medicines and other chemicals shall he provided.
Facilities for the humane destruction of animals or fowl and the appropriate means for disposal of the remains shall
he provided.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 4.04)
Sec. 6-90. - Humane treatment of animals required.
Animals under impoundment shall be treated in a humane manner. They shall he provided reasonable protection from
extremes in weather. Animals suspected of having a communicable disease shall be isolated from the remainder of the animal
population. Each animal shall be fed an adequate amount of food at least once per day, and shall have fresh water available at all
reasonable times.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 4.05)
Sec. 6-91. - Recordkeeping.
Records shall be kept at the pound and will, at a minimum, include:
A description of each animal;
The date and time it was taken into custody;
Notations as to efforts to identify and notify the owner;
Rabies inoculation status and any other pertinent medical information;
To whom the animal was released and the charges assessed and by whom laid; and
If the animal was not released, the date of disposal.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 4.06)
Sec. 6-92. - Fees.
The city council may establish fees for:
The apprehension of any animals running at large;
The impoundment of animals at the city animal shelter;
The redemption of animals impounded under the provisions of this division; and
The disposal of animals not claimed or adopted.
Such fees shall be sufficient for the city to recover the costs incurred in the administration of this chapter. These

ARTICLE IV. - CONFINEMENT, VACCINATION REQUIREMENTS AND PROHIBITED CONDITIONS
Sec. 6-113. - At large animal declared nuisance.
No person owning, having an interest in, harboring or having the care, charge control, or possession of any animal
shall permit or allow it (either willfully or through failure to exercise due care of control) to be, remain, go, or run at
large upon a public right-of-way park or other public space or any open lot or land in the city other than on the
property of the said animal's owner. The presence of any animal upon a public right-of-way, park or other public
space or upon any open lot or land in the city other than on the property of the said animal's owner, is hereby
declared to be a nuisance and dangerous to the public health and safety.
All animals found to be at large in violation of this chapter may be impounded in the manner proscribed in this
chapter.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 3.01)
Sec. 6-114. - Vaccination of animals—Required.
Evidence. It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep or harbor any canine or feline which has not been
vaccinated against rabies as required by the rules and regulations established in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 31-19-5.
Evidence of such vaccination shall consist of:
A certificate bearing the owner's name and address;
Number of the vaccination tag issued;
Date of the vaccination;
Date the animal shall be revaccinated;
Type and lot number of the vaccine administered; and
The signature of the person administering the vaccine.
Copies. The certificate shall be prepared in triplicate, the original given to the owner, the first copy filed in the office
of the county board of health, and the second copy retained by the person administering the vaccine.
Veterinary supervision needed. All vaccinations shall be administered by or under the supervision of a veterinarian
licensed by the Georgia Board of Veterinary Medical Examiners to practice veterinary medicine in the state or by
other persons qualified under state law for that purpose.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 3.02)
Sec. 6-115. - Same—Proof by wearing tag.
All animals required to be vaccinated under section 6-114 shall wear the vaccination tag issued for the current year in a clearly
visible location.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 3.03)
Sec. 6-116. - Display of vaccination certicate required upon demand.

No person keeping or harboring an animal shall fail or refuse to exhibit a certificate of vaccination required by this chapter
upon demand of the animal control officer, health department representative, police officer or any other city official.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 3.04)
Sec. 6-117. - Nuisance procedure.
No person shall allow any animal over which they have custody or control to remain on their property or premises if
the same shall constitute a nuisance.
The council, upon formal complaint by any citizen concerning an animal, shall conduct an investigation to determine
whether the animal constitutes a nuisance. If the council determines that the animal does constitute a nuisance, the
owner of the animal shall be so notified and shall be given a reasonable period of time during which to correct
those conditions constituting the nuisance. Failure to correct said nuisance within a period of time considered
reasonable by the council shall be punishable as prescribed in general penalty section 1-7
(Code 1973, § 4-17; Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 3.05)

ARTICLE V. - RABIES CONTROL
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (2) ---
State Law reference— Rabies control, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-1 et seq.
Sec. 6-148. - Duty to surrender body of animal suspected of rabies.
It shall the duty of the owner or person having custody of any animal suspected of having rabies to surrender the carcass of
the animal, or such portion of the carcass as may be requested, to the animal control officer after the death of the animal.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.06)
Sec. 6-149. - Quarantine required.
All veterinarians treating an animal indicating symptoms of rabies shall hold such animal in quarantine until the disposition of
said animal by the animal control officer.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.07)
Sec. 6-150. - Duty to report animal biting animal incident.
It shall be the duty of every person having knowledge of any animal that bites another animal to report immediately to the city
animal control department the following information:
The existence and description of such animal;
The place where the biting incident occurred;
The owner's name, if known;
A description of the animal that was bitten; and
The owner's name, if known.

(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.08)
Sec. 6-151. - Management—Animals that scratch or bite humans.
Dogs and cats. A healthy dog or cat that bites or scratches a person or another animal should be confined and
observed for ten days. This required quarantine applies to dogs and cats only. A rabies vaccine should not be
administered during the observation period. While in confinement, any signs of illness should be evaluated by a
licensed veterinarian. The place of confinement shall be at the agency designated by the city council as the animal
shelter at the expense of the owner or person having custody or possession of the animal the veterinarian chosen
by the owner or person having the custody or possession of the animal at said owner's expense, or any other
confinement location so designated and approved by the animal control officer. If symptoms suggestive of rabies
are observed, the animal should be humanely killed, and a specimen should be submitted to a qualified laboratory
for testing. If the animal dies during the quarantine period, the specimen should be submitted immediately for
rabies testing.
Stray domestic animals and other species. Any stray or unwanted animal that bites or scratches a person or
domestic animal may be humanely euthanized and a specimen submitted for testing. Animals other than dogs or
cats that bite or scratch a person and are suspected of being rabid should immediately be reported to the city
animal control department. Management of animals other than dogs and cats is dependent on the animal species,
the circumstances of the bite, and the epidemiology of rabies in the area, and shall be at the discretion of the animal
control officer or the county health department or their authorized representative.
Livestock. Cattle, horses, mules, donkeys, goats, swine and sheep are not likely to be reservoirs of rabies. Treatment
will be weighed against the circumstances of exposure by the animal control officer (if the county health
department or its authorized representative). If at the time of exposure the animal is clinically ill with signs
suggestive of rabies, the animal control officer or his authorized representative, or an authorized representative
from the county health department will immediately and humanely kill the animal and a specimen will lie submitted
to a qualified laboratory for testing. The cost of testing will be the responsibility of the animal owner, if known.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.09)
Sec. 6-152. - Same—Animals exposed to rabies.
Any animal bitten or scratched by a bat or wild carnivorous mammal (particularly bobcat, raccoon, fox, skunk, or coyote) which
is not available for testing should be considered exposed to rabies.
Unvaccinated dogs and cats. Unvaccinated or unwanted dogs and cats bitten or scratched by a known or
potentially rabid animal should be humanely euthanized immediately. If the owner of the animal is unwilling to
have this done (upon approval of the department head of the city animal control) the exposed animal must be
placed in strict isolation for six months and vaccinated one month prior to being released. The responsibility
for isolation of an exposed unvaccinated animal remains with the owner animal must be kept in a pen that has
been built to the specifications of the State of Georgia Rabies Control Manual Appendix C, and approved by the
department head of the city animal control and the chief animal control officer. Additionally, a second fence 18
inches to 24 inches in distance from the inner pen must be erected around the perimeter to guarantee
complete isolation of the quarantined animal from other animals and human contact. The total construction
costs of this confinement area is the sole responsibility of the pet owner. Previously vaccinated dogs and cats
whose rabies vaccination has lapsed for more than 30 days are considered unvaccinated and will be treated as
such.
Vaccinated dogs and cats. Dogs and cats that are currently vaccinated (vaccinated at least one month prior to
exposure) should be revaccinated immediately confined and observed for 45 days. Confinement must be
coordinated with and approved by the city animal control and/or the county health department.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
55/192
(3)
(4)

(b)
(c)
Livestock. Vaccinated livestock (vaccinated by a licensed veterinarian with a USDA approved vaccine for that speci
days prior to the attack) bitten by a rabid animal should be revaccinated immediately, confined, and observed for
Confinement must be coordinated with and approved by the city animal control and/or the county health departm
Other animals. Unvaccinated animals bitten by a rabid animal should be euthanized immediately. If an animal
has been vaccinated with a USDA approved vaccine for the species, the animal must be revaccinated
immediately and placed in confinement for a minimum of 90 days. Confinement must be coordinated with and
approved by the city animal control and/or the county health department.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.10)
Sec. 6-153. - Quarantine of area.
Whenever in the judgment of the city council, after consultation with the city animal control and the county health department,
the public health and safety so require the council shall declare and establish a quarantine zone or area consisting of the whole or
any part of the city, and maintain such quarantine therein until such time as they may deem it advisable to lift the same. During the
existence of such quarantine, it shall be unlawful for any person to violate any of the rules and regulations proscribed by the city
council, with reference to such quarantine.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.11)
Sec. 6-154. - Retention of animals suspected of having rabies.
If the animal control officer or poundkeeper for the agency operating a pound for the city suspects that any animal
impounded has rabies he shall notify the city animal control department. A qualified veterinarian shall examine
such animal and if they believe such animal should be held for future observation, they shall so inform the animal
control officer.
If an animal does not have rabies, the animal control officer or agency operating a pound for the city shall release it
or dispose of it in the manner proscribed in this chapter.
After observation by a veterinarian licensed to practice in the state, if symptoms suggestive rabies are observed, the
animal should be humanely killed, its head carefully removed and shipped on ice for examination by the state public
health laboratory. If the animal dies during the quarantine period, the head shall be submitted immediately for
rabies testing. If the animal lives through the duration of the quarantine and no symptoms of rabies are observed
that animal shall be released to the owner or turned over to the agency operating the city's animal shelter.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.12)
Sec. 6-155. - Animal exposed to rabies barred from city.
No person shall bring any animal into the city in which rabies has been present within six months prior thereto.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 5.13)
Secs. 6-156—6-178. - Reserved.
ARTICLE VI. - DANGEROUS DOGS
FOOTNOTE(S):

State Law reference— Dangerous Dog Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-20; vicious dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-40 et seq.

Sec. 6-179. - Purpose.
The purpose of this article is to clearly define local government responsibility, as well as limit the administrative and
liability burdens upon the city with regard to potentially dangerous and dangerous dogs.
A dog that inflicts an injury upon a person when the dog is being used by a law enforcement officer to carry out the
law enforcement officer's official duties shall not be a dangerous dog or a potentially dangerous dog within the
meaning of this article. A dog shall not be a dangerous dog or a potentially dog within the meaning of this article if
the injury inflicted by the dog was sustained by a person who, at the time, was committing a willful trespass or other
tort or was tormenting, abusing, or assaulting the dog or had in the past been observed or reported to have
tormented, abused, or assaulted the dog or was committing or attempting to commit a crime.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 7.01)
Sec. 6-180. - Dog control ocer—Designated.
The chief animal control officer of the city shall also be designated as the dog control officer for purposes of this article. It shall
be the dog control officer's duty to investigate and classify as appropriate suspected dangerous or potentially dangerous dogs.
However, the dog control officer's duty of investigation and classification only arises when a report of an occurrence justifying said
classification occurs in the incorporated portions of the city from any law enforcement agency, rabies control office, county or state
board of health, or a written report by a citizen of the city.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 7.02)
Sec. 6-181. - Same—Responsibilities.
Investigation and classification. Upon receiving a report that a dog has acted in dangerous or potentially dangerous
manner, the dog control officer shall investigate the allegations and make a determination as to the truthfulness of
said allegations. After concluding the investigation, the dog control officer shall:
Decide if the classification of the dog as dangerous or potentially dangerous is not required; or
Classify the dog as potentially dangerous.
Notice. In the event that the dog control officer classifies the dog under investigation as dangerous or potentially
dangerous, the dog control officer must notify the owner by certified mail. The notice shall include a summary of the
reason for which the animal has been classified and provide the owners with a form to request a hearing to contest
the classification within 15 days of the notice date. If no hearing is requested, the dog's classification goes into effect
on the 15th day.
Hearing. An owner who requests a hearing under subsection (b) of this section shall be provided a hearing before
the animal control board within 30 days. The owners must be notified of the hearing date, time and location by
certified mail. The hearing shall be conducted such that owners have the opportunity to present their testimony,
cross examine witnesses, and present evidence. The animal control board shall receive such other evidence and
hear such other testimony as is reasonably necessary to make a determination to either sustain, modify, or overrule
the dog control officer's classification of the dog. Within ten days after the hearing, the animal control board shall
make a final determination as to the classification of the dog and provide notice of its determination by certified
mail to the owners. In the event that the animal control board, after a hearing, classifies a dog as dangerous or
potentially' dangerous the effective date of such classification, which shall be the date the decision is made, must be
given.
(Ord. of 1-4-1999, § 7.03)

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 8-1. - Exemption from water saving plumbing device requirements.
New construction and the repair or renovation of an existing building shall be exempt from the requirements of
O.C.G.A. § 8-3-2(c) when:
The repair or renovation of the existing building does not include the replacement of the plumbing or
sewerage system servicing toilets, faucets or showerheads within such existing buildings;
When such plumbing or sewerage system within such existing building, because of its capacity, design, or
installation would not function properly if the toilets, faucets or showerheads required by this chapter were
installed;
Such system is a well or gravity flow from a spring and is owned privately by an individual for use in such
individual's personal residence; or
Units to be installed are:
Specifically designed for use by persons with disabilities;
Specifically designed it withstand unusual abuse or installation in a penal institution; or
Toilets for juveniles.
The owner, or his agent, of a building undergoing new construction or repair or renovation, who is entitled to an
exemption as specified in subsection (a)(2), (3) or (4) of this section, shall obtain the exemption by applying at the
office of the building inspector for the city. A fee in an amount as established from time to time by the city shall be
charged for the inspection and issuance of such exemption.
(Ord. of 6-10-1991, § 5)
Sec. 8-2. - Dangerous buildings.

power to repair, close or demolish such dwellings, buildings, or structures in the manner provided in O.C.G.A. §§ 41-
2-8 through 41-2-17. The provisions of O.C.G.A. §§ 41-2-7 through 41-2-17 are hereby adopted and incorporated by
reference as if fully set forth in this chapter.
Police chief designated to enforce chapter. The city chief of police is hereby designated as the public officer
authorized to exercise powers prescribed in the statutes adopted in this section.
Findings of fact. It is found that there exist in the city dwellings, buildings and structures which are unfit for human
habitation or for commercial, industrial or business uses due to:
Dilapidation and defects increasing the hazards of fire, accident, or other calamities;
The lack of adequate ventilation, light or sanitary facilities; or
Other conditions rendering such dwellings, buildings or structures unsafe or unsanitary, or dangerous or
detrimental to the health, safety or welfare, or otherwise inimical to the welfare of the residents of the city.
(Ord. of 12-10-1990(1), §§ 1, 2; Ord. of 12-10-1990(2), §§ 1, 2)

Sec. 8-23. - Failure to comply; ne.
Failure to comply with this article is a misdemeanor. The police department or their designee may cause to be
issued an arrest warrant, or summons to appear before the municipal court to answer such alleged violation. A
summons to appear may be served upon an alleged violator either in person or by certified mail.
The minimum fine for a violation of this article shall be $25.00 plus court costs.
(Ord. of 3-10-2003)
Sec. 8-24. - Scheme.
The city has established a new address numbering system, which shall be administered by the Early-Calhoun 911
Department.
Each house, building, or other occupiable structure shall be assigned a separate number. A number or alphabetical
letter shall be assigned for each separate and distinct occupant or division (i.e., apartment, company, etc.) within a
building or other occupied structure.
Existing numbers shall be changed only as necessary to ensure the effectiveness or efficiency of the Enhanced 911
System of Early-Calhoun County, as determined by the judgment of the Early-Calhoun 911 Department.
All new buildings and structures must be assigned a numbered address by the Early-Calhoun 911 Department, prior
to or simultaneous with the granting of: a building permit, septic tank permit, electrical permit, or connecting to any
city gas, water or sewerage line.
Written notification of the address assigned under the terms of this article to each house, building, or structure shall
be given or delivered to its respective owner/occupant.
Written notification of the address assigned under the terms of this article to each house, building or structure shall
also be given to the U.S. Postal 911 Address Coordinator.
(Ord. of 3-10-2003)
Sec. 8-25. - Placement.
The owner, occupant, or agent of each house, building or business shall display the assigned number on the
structure no later than March 31, 2003.
The Early-Calhoun 911 Department will supply the numbers for all structures one time, any subsequent numbers
required will be the responsibility of the property owner. The property owner, occupant, or agent of each house,
building, or other structure, shall be responsible for installation of the numbers.
Residential numbers shall be conspicuously placed immediately to the right side of the appropriate door, so that the
number is clearly visible from the street, and/or the building number may be placed near the walk, driveway, or
common entrance to the building, or placed on the mailbox, gatepost, or other appropriate place, so as to be clearly
visible from the street.
(Ord. of 3-10-2003)
Sec. 8-26. - Defacing, altering, destroying, concealing or removing numbers.
Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to deface, alter, destroy, conceal or remove any 911 address
numbers, except by the owner, occupant, or agent, as required for maintenance, upkeep and replacement as
required, to maintain the numbers in good readable condition.
Fine. The minimum fine for a violation of this section shall be $100.00 plus court costs.
(Ord. of 3-10-2003)
