They shall also have such special police officers as may be designated by the city council to assist them when
necessary in the discharge of their duties.
It shall be the duty of the chief of police to attend all meetings of the council and preserve order.
It shall be the duty of the police officers of the city to arrest and bring before the municipal court or other
proper authority all violators, of the laws of the state, or the Charter or ordinances of the city which may come
to their knowledge, when such violations shall be within the city.
To arrest and carry before the proper officer for examination all offenders against the state laws committed in
their presence. To arrest and confine in the county jail any offender against the ordinances in the city or take
bond with good security. When such arrest and confinement is necessary to secure the appearance of such
offender before the municipal court, he may arrest without warrant.
To preserve order in the city, to take up all drunken, disorderly or riotous persons who are disturbing the
peace and quiet of the city, and to commit them to the county jail, there to remain until sufficient bond is given
and shall then bring said offender before the next session of the municipal court to be dealt with as evidence
produced shall warrant. In case of his inability to suppress such disorders, or to disperse riotous assemblages,
he shall have the power to call to his assistance a sufficient number of persons to aid him in so doing.
To call upon the mayor, or in his absence, the mayor pro-tem, to ascertain if there are any commands to
execute, and he shall at the same time report all infractions of city ordinances within his knowledge, for the
information and action of the mayor. To guard the city from fire, and on the appearance of fire, to give a fire
alarm. He shall protect persons and property.
To keep sober and free from intoxication or the influence of liquor.
To make out a complete list of all business houses, professions, and occupations subject to licenses and to
return the same to the city clerk.
To make weekly settlements with the city clerk and to pay over to the clerk upon each settlement the amount
of money in his hands.
To perform such other duties as may be required of him by the city council.
(Code 1973, § 12-5)
Chapter 22 - LICENSES, TAXATION AND MISCELLANEOUS BUSINESS REGULATIONS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 22-1. - Tax ordinances passed each year.
The city council shall pass, each year, such tax ordinances, not contrary to law, as it may deem proper.
(Code 1973, § 14-1)
Sec. 22-2. - All property taxable.
Each person owning or having control in his own right or as agent or otherwise of any real property in the city, or owning or
having control of any money, solvent notes or accounts, as the property of any citizen of the city, shall pay a tax upon the full value
thereof, at such a percentage as may be fixed by the city council in each year.
(Code 1973, § 14-2)
Sec. 22-3. - Return—Date.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances

Each person subject to taxation in the city, owning or having possession or control in his own right or for the use of any person
as parent, guardian, trustee, executor, administrator or agent, or in any other manner whatever, shall make to the assessors on or
before March 31 in each year a full, true and complete return of all property taxable by the city, including all trades, businesses,

(Code 1973, § 14-3)
Sec. 22-4. - Same—Oath or armation.
The person making a tax return, either for himself or in any representative capacity, shall be required, on making the same, to
take the following oath or affirmation: "I do solemnly swear (or affirm) that the return which I have now made is a just, full and
complete return of all property, businesses, trades, professions and occupations, in my own right and as parent, guardian,
executor, administrator, agent or trustee, or in any other manner, whatever, subject to taxation under the Ordinances of the City of
Edison, which I owned, had possession of or controlled in my own right, or the right of any other person or company whosoever,
on the first day of January last past, and the value of the same is not more than I have affixed to the best of my knowledge and
belief, so help me God."
(Code 1973, § 14-4)
Sec. 22-5. - False or incomplete return prohibited; penalty.
Any person who shall knowingly make a false or incomplete city tax return shall, on conviction be punished as prescribed in
general penalty section 1-7.
(Code 1973, § 14-5)
Sec. 22-6. - Double tax assessment for failing to make return.
Any person failing to make his city tax return shall be liable for a double tax to be assessed by the assessors upon the basis of
the tax paid by such defaulter for the preceding year, or upon the best estimate the assessors are able to make of the taxable
property of the defaulter. The city clerk shall report to the assessors all defaulters.
(Code 1973, § 14-6)
Sec. 22-7. - Taxes paid to city clerk.
All city taxes shall be paid to the city clerk, and by him paid to the treasurer, at such time as shall be called for by the city
council in each year.
(Code 1973, § 14-7)
Sec. 22-8. - Tax digest.
Duty of clerk to maintain. It shall be the duty of the city clerk to keep a correct and proper digest of all taxable
property in the city.
Contents. The digest shall contain the description, valuation and class of property returned and the names of
person returning the same.
Deadline for renewal and completion. The digest is to be renewed and completed by September 1 in each year.
Examination by city council. Upon completion of the digest, the city clerk shall turn the same over to the city council,
whose duty it shall be to examine the same, and if found correct, to return the same to the clerk.

ARTICLE II. - FIRE PROTECTION SPECIAL TAX DISTRICT
Sec. 22-35. - Created.
There is hereby created pursuant to article IX, section II, paragraph VI of the state constitution a special tax district which shall
be known as "City of Edison Fire Protection Tax District," hereinafter referred to as "the district."
(Ord. of 4-12-2010, § 1)
Sec. 22-36. - Boundaries.
The district boundaries shall be all the property situate, lying and being in the incorporated areas of the city.
(Ord. of 4-12-2010, § 2)
Sec. 22-37. - Imposition and collection of taxes.
The minimum fee for each active residential unit and commercial unit located in the district provided city water
services shall be $2.00 per month. Fees in excess of the minimum shall be based on a schedule for services
provided as adopted by the city council. Fees for subsequent years shall be set annually by the city council at its first
regular meeting of each fiscal year.
The owner of the active residential or commercial unit as determined from the published tax digest for the city or
water service recipient shall be billed for the fee to be collected. Said fee shall be collected for the entire tax year
against the listed owner or recipient of water services unless and council is provided with the name, address and
copy of the deed of conveyance. The fee shall be collected from the new owner or recipient of water services
commencing upon the first month following the conveyance, provided the information contained in this section is
received on or before the 20th of the month of the conveyance or on the first of the second month next that if
received after the 20th of the month of conveyance.
All active units shall be defined as all occupied single-family or multifamily dwelling units including mobile homes
and modular units receiving billable water services. Multifamily structures such as duplexes and apartment
buildings shall be billed as to each individual unit contained therein. All commercial units shall be defined as any
hotel, motel, restaurant, business, public or semi-public establishment of any kind receiving water services.
Said fee shall be due and payable by the 20th of each month. A late payment penalty and an assessment of interest
shall be imposed upon each account for which a payment is not made within the prescribed time limits.
The fees for collection of residential or commercial fire protection levied pursuant to the terms of this article, and all
late charges and interest accruing thereon are hereby deemed and constituted a tax and are hereby levied severally
against the owner and occupant of each residential unit, including all residential units located in mobile home
courts and/or trailer courts. The fees, late charges and interest prescribed in this section shall be determined and
treated in all respects as provided by law with respect to ad valorem and state taxes.
Uncollected fees, late charges and interest shall constitute a continuing lien:
Against the real property upon which each residential unit is located;
Upon the personal property composing a residential unit; and
Upon the personal property of the occupant of each residential unit, until paid.
Writs of fi. fas. may be issued by the city for fees which are past due and collection may be effected as provided by
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
95/192
law for ad valorem or other state taxes, as provided by O.C.G.A. § 48-5-359.
(Ord. of 4-12-2010, § 3)
Sec. 22-38. - Disposition of proceeds.
All taxes and fees imposed by this article shall be used and appropriated to pay for fire protection in the district. Said taxes
and fees shall be deposited in a special account set up by the city specifically for this purpose.
(Ord. of 4-12-2010, § 4)
Secs. 22-39—22-64. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - BUSINESS LICENSE TAXES AND FEES
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 22-65. - Engaging in business without paying license fee or tax prohibited; penalty.
It shall not be lawful for any person of whom a tax or license is required to commence or engage in the business, trade,
profession, occupation or pursuit that may be taxed, or license required, until registering, as required, paying the tax or license and
complying with the requirements imposed in this Code. Anyone offending shall be punished as prescribed in general penalty
section 1-7.
(Code 1973, § 14-9)
Sec. 22-66. - License to be signed by mayor; recordkeeping; transferable with city council's consent.
No license shall be valid until signed by the city clerk. The city clerk shall keep in a book a record of all licenses issued. No
license shall be issued for a period to extend beyond the next December 31. Each license is valid and good only to the person to
whom issued and shall not be transferred without the consent of the city council.
(Code 1973, § 14-26)
Secs. 22-67—22-90. - Reserved.

State Law reference— Local taxes and fees on insurance companies and agents, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8 et seq.
Sec. 22-91. - License fees levied on life insurers—Generally.
There is hereby levied an annual license fee upon each life insurer doing business within the city in the amount of $25.00. For
each separate business location in excess of one not covered by section 22-92, which is operating on behalf of such insurers within
the city, there is hereby levied a license fee in the amount of $25.00. For the purposes of this division, the term "insurer" means a
company which is authorized to transact business in the class of insurance designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5(1).
(Ord. of 11-14-1983, § 1)
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
96/192
State law reference— Authority for above fee, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.
Sec. 22-92. - Same—Insuring certain risks at additional business locations.
For each separate business location, not otherwise subject to a license fee under this division, operated and maintained by a
business organization which is engaged in the business of lending money or transacting sales involving term financing and in
connection with such loans or sales, offers, solicits or takes applications for insurance through a licensed agent of a life insurer for
life insurance, said insurer shall pay an additional license fee of $10.00 per location each year.
(Ord. of 11-14-1983, § 2)
State law reference— Authority for above fee, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.
Sec. 22-93. - Life insurance agency license fees; independent life insurance agencies, brokers, etc., not otherwise licensed.
There is hereby levied an annual license fee upon independent agencies and brokers for each separate business location from
which a life insurance business is conducted, and which is not subject to the company license fee imposed by section 22-91, in the
amount of $15.00 for each such location within the city.
(Ord. of 11-14-1983, § 3)
State law reference— Authority for above fee, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.
Sec. 22-94. - Gross premiums tax—Imposed on life insurers.
There is hereby levied an annual tax based solely upon gross direct premiums upon each insurer writing life, accident and
sickness insurance within the city in an amount equal to one percent of the gross direct premiums received during the calendar
year in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.1, except that such tax shall not apply to the gross direct premiums of an insurance
company which qualifies, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 33-8-5, for the reduction to one-half percent of the state tax imposed by O.C.G.A. §
33-8-4. The tax imposed by this section shall not apply to annuity considerations. As used in this section, the term "gross direct
premiums" means the definition used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-4. The premium tax levied by this section is in addition to the license fees
imposed by section 22-91.
(Ord. of 11-14-1983, § 4)
Sec. 22-95. - Same—Levied upon all other insurers.
There is hereby levied an annual tax upon each insurer, other than an insurer transacting business in the class of insurance
designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5(1), doing business within the city in an amount equal to 2½ percent of the gross direct premiums
received during the calendar year in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2. As used in this section, the term "gross direct premiums"
means the definition used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2(a).
(Ord. of 11-14-1983, § 5)
Sec. 22-96. - Due date for license fees.
The license fees imposed in sections 22-91, 22-92 and 22-93 shall be due and payable on the first day of 1984 and on the first
of each subsequent year.
(Ord. of 11-14-1983, § 6)

Secs. 22-146—22-173. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - PERMIT
Sec. 22-174. - Required.
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell any magazine, periodical, book or newspaper, or to solicit or sell subscriptions
thereto, within the city without having first obtained from the city a permit therefor, except that this requirement shall not be
imposed upon any person duly enrolled in a public or private school located in the county when such a person is engaged in a
school approved project, or a project sponsored by a recognized civic, charitable, or fraternal organization.
(Code 1973, § 11-1)
Sec. 22-175. - Application; investigation and recommendation by chief of police required.
Any person desiring to sell, or solicit subscription to, any magazine, periodical, book or newspaper, within the city shall apply to
the city clerk for a permit to do so. The city clerk shall thereupon file the application and refer it to the chief of police, who shall
investigate the applicant and the type of periodical, magazine, newspaper or book, and recommend to the city clerk whether the
permit should be granted or refused.
(Code 1973, § 11-2)
Sec. 22-176. - Council action.
The city clerk shall, within five days after the recommendation of the chief of police on the granting or refusing a permit
required in section 22-174 has been submitted, submit such recommendation to the council, which shall act thereon. The council
shall consider such recommendation, and all the facts pertaining thereto, and shall either grant the permit or refuse same.
(Code 1973, § 11-3)

ARTICLE V. - POOL OR BILLIARD ROOMS
Sec. 22-206. - Conditions for issuance of license; fee.
A pool or billiard room may be licensed to do business in the city upon the payment of the annual specific business license as
provided for in this article; provided that this license shall be issued under and subject to the following conditions:
The licensee or operator shall not permit or allow any conduct that is in violation of any ordinance in said pool
or billiard room.
The licensee or operator shall not permit or allow any gambling in any form, whether the same be betting on
the games played therein, craps, poker, or any game of chance for money or other thing or things of value.
The licensee or operator shall not permit any person under the influence of intoxicating drink, beverage or
drug to remain in said place of business, but if and in the event any person under the influence of intoxicating
drink, beverage or drug shall come into said pool or billiard room the operator or person in charge thereof,
shall immediately evict said person or call the city police and have him evicted. The term "under the influence
of intoxicating drink, beverage or drug" means to any degree, the state courts having defined a person that has
taken one drink as being under the influence of said beverage to that extent.
No person shall be allowed or permitted to bring into said pool or billiard room any intoxicating drink of any
kind, or any beer or wine of any percent alcohol content.
No pool or billiard room shall be open for business between the hours of 12:00 midnight on Saturday night
and 6:00 a.m. on Monday morning. The opening of said place of business between said hours shall be prima
facie evidence that said pool or billiard room is open for the conduct of business.
No person shall be permitted or allowed to violate any city ordinance or state law in said pool or billiard room.
(Ord. of 12-8-1980, ¶ 5)
Sec. 22-207. - Prima facie evidence of violation.
The fact that any city ordinance, condition stated in section 22-206 under which the license is granted, or state law is violated
in said pool room shall be prima facie evidence that the same was allowed by the operator or licensee and is in violation of the
conditions under which said license is granted. The pool room or billiard room license as issued under and subject to the
conditions stated in section 22-206, regulations and ordinances of the city or state law, is valid so long as none of the above are
violated, and said license is purchased and accepted by the licensee under said conditions.
(Ord. of 12-8-1980, ¶ 5)
Sec. 22-208. - Suspension and revocation.
In the event any of the conditions, regulations, or ordinances are violated in said pool room or billiard room, or any disorderly
conduct shall take place therein, it shall be the duty of the mayor to suspend said license and order the city police to close said
place of business until the next regular meeting of the city council, and at said meeting if the council shall find that any of the
conditions mentioned in section 22-206, regulations and ordinances of the city have been violated therein, said license shall be
revoked instanter, and none of the license money refunded to said licensee or operator.
(Ord. of 12-8-1980, ¶ 5)
Sec. 22-209. - Acceptance of conditions and terms; copies of article; display of license.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
102/192
(a)
(b)
(c)
(d)
The purchase of any license to operate a pool room or billiard room shall be conclusive evidence that the purchaser thereof
accepts and purchases the license under the terms and conditions heretofore set forth in this article, and it shall be the duty of the
city clerk to furnish every person buying such license with a copy of this article and the purchaser shall keep same posted in a
conspicuous place in said pool or billiard room at all times.
(Ord. of 12-8-1980, ¶ 5)
Chapter 24 - MUNICIPAL COURT
FOOTNOTE(S):
--- (1) ---
State Law reference— Municipal courts, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-1 et seq.
Sec. 24-1. - Time of holding court; strict rules of criminal procedure used; accusations; appearance.
It shall be the duty of the judge, or in his absence the judge pro-tem, to hold court whenever it becomes necessary for the trial
and punishment of violators of city ordinances. Strict rules of criminal procedure as enforced in the courts of law shall not be
necessary in the municipal court. Defendants shall be tried upon written or printed accusations. Every defendant shall have the
right of appearing and pleading by counsel or by himself, or by both.
(Code 1973, § 6-1; Ord. of 12-13-1982(1))
Sec. 24-2. - Indigent defense services.
Application required; contents. Each person lacking the financial ability to provide, for themselves, representation in
his defense in criminal proceedings in the municipal court, and desiring that the city provide such services to him,
shall submit an application to the city requesting indigent defense representation and setting forth the specifics
supporting their need for such indigent representation.
Public defender. The application shall be submitted to the public defender upon first appearance on a form
approved by the city council.
Application fee—Required. Each applicant for indigent defense service shall pay an application fee in an amount as
established from time to time by the city to the public defender of municipal court. Such fee must be paid either at
the time the application is submitted or at the time the representation is provided.
Same—Waiver. The fee required by subsection (c) of this section may be waived only upon order of the presiding
judge scheduled to hear the case in which the applicant is seeking a waiver of the application fee. The judge may
order a waiver of the fee only upon a finding by the court that the defendant is unable to pay the fee or that paying
the fee would cause hardship to the defendant.
(Ord. of 3-28-2005(2), §§ 1—3)
State law reference— Authority for above fee, O.C.G.A. § 15-21A-6(e).
Sec. 24-3. - Contents, issuance and service—Summons.
It shall be the duty of the chief of police, in all cases, when a complaint is made or information given of any violation of the
laws or ordinances of the city, whether the party be confined or not, to issue a summons directed to the accused, requiring said
offender to appear before the municipal court to answer said charge, which summons shall contain the offense and time and place
of trial, bear teste in the name of the judge, be signed officially by the chief of police and directed to any public officer of the city to
be executed, which officer shall execute the same by serving a copy upon the accused, or leaving it at his place of residence.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
103/192
(1)
(2)
(3)
(Code 1973, § 6-3; Ord. of 12-13-1982(1))
Sec. 24-4. - Same—Witness subpoena.
Whenever the attendance of any witness may be required before the municipal court to establish any fact, the chief of police
shall issue a subpoena, as directed to the witness, stating the time and place of trial and the parties to the case, which shall bear
teste in the name of the judge and be served as other summons by any member of the city police force.
(Code 1973, § 6-5; Ord. of 12-13-1982(1))
Sec. 24-5. - Penalty for contempt.
Any person who, during the sitting of the municipal court, shall be guilty of a contempt of court or refuse to abide by any
sentence or order of said court, shall be fined in the sum not exceeding $25.00 and costs, or confinement in the county jail not
exceeding 24 hours for each offense.
(Code 1973, § 6-9)
Sec. 24-6. - Execution for nes.
The chief of police shall issue an execution instanter when any fine is imposed by the municipal court, to be levied upon the
goods, chattels, lands and tenements of the person so fined, if the sum is not immediately paid, which execution shall bear teste in
the name of the mayor and be signed officially by the chief of police and be directed to the chief of police, to all and singular the
sheriffs and their deputies of this state.
(Code 1973, § 6-10)
Sec. 24-7. - Duties of municipal court clerk.
The duties of the municipal court clerk are as follows:
To keep a docket wherein shall be entered the names of all persons tried and fined by the municipal court, the
nature of the offense, date of trial, amount of the fine, and return of the police officer thereon, the same to be
laid before the city council at each regular meeting.
To attend all sessions of the municipal court, and any other business of the municipal court as required.
To keep a book of minutes and a docket of the municipal court.
(Code 1973, § 2-29(3), (5), (9)f.)

Sec. 26-19. - Prohibited odors.
It shall be unlawful for any owner or individual in control of any property within the boundaries of the city to:
Allow the accumulation of animal body wastes;
Boil offal, bone, fat, tallow;
Manufacture glue, varnish or oil;
Make lamp black, turpentine or tar;
Distill alcoholic spirits;
Render or dry out dead animals; or
Conduct any other activity, business or trade not specifically enumerated in this Code whereby noisome
stenches and odors arise, or noxious gases are generated or circulated within the city.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-20. - Obstructions to cross visibility.
In order to promote and conserve the public health and safety and pursuant to the police powers of the city and the
power to prevent and abate public nuisances as conferred upon the city by the laws of the state, it is hereby
declared to be a public nuisance for a person owning and/or having the legal control of any land within the
corporate limits of the city to maintain or permit upon any such land any fence, sign, billboard, shrubbery, bush,
tree, mailbox or other object, or any combination thereof which obstructs the view of motorists using any street or
approach to any street intersection so as to constitute a traffic hazard or a condition dangerous to the public safety.
The restrictions set forth in this section shall apply to both of the following triangles of land:
The triangle bounded by the curb edged (or edges of pavement where there is no curb), measured along the
curb edge (or edge of the pavement where there is no curb) 20 feet from the midpoint of the radius of the curb
edge (or edge of pavement where there is no curb) in each direction and the diagonal line connecting the
further ends of such 20-foot lengths; and
The triangle bounded by the right-of-way lines measured 15 feet from the point of their intersection in each
direction and the diagonal line connecting the further ends of such 15-foot lengths.
Within said triangles, and except as provided in subsection (d) of this section, it shall be unlawful to install, set out or
maintain, or allow the installation, setting out, or maintenance of, any sign, hedge, shrubbery, tree, natural growth,
earthen berm, or other object of any kind which obstructs cross-visibility at a level between 30 inches and 72 inches
above the level or the center of the adjacent intersection which obstructs the view of motorist using any street or
approach to any street intersection so as to constitute a traffic hazard or a condition dangerous to the public safety.
The provision of subsections (c) of this section shall not apply to:
Permanent buildings and permanent additions thereto.
Existing natural grades which, by reason of natural topography, rise 30 or more inches above the level of the
center of the adjacent intersection.
Trees having limbs and foliage trimmed in such manner that no limbs or foliage extends into the area between
30 inches and 72 inches above the level of the center of the adjacent intersection.
Fire hydrants, public utility poles, street markers, government signs, and traffic control devices.
Where compliance with this section described triangles or at the heights described alone is insufficient to prevent a
dangerous condition, the city public works superintendent may designate further measure which must be taken by
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances

the owner or other responsible person to eliminate such dangerous condition. Such measures shall be designed to
provide an adequate sight and stopping distance for person approaching the intersection at prevailing speeds and
may include the removal of obstruction at different heights or in area outside the triangles established in subsection
(b) of this section.
The administration of this section shall be under the direction of the city public works superintendent who shall
investigate violations, issue such notices and orders as are required in this article, and perform such other duties as
may be necessary to the enforcement thereof.
Any obstruction to cross visibility maintained in violation of this section shall be deemed a public nuisance
inconsistent with and detrimental to the public safety and shall be abated in accordance with the following
procedure:
The city public works superintendent shall cause to be served by certified mail a written notice and order of
abatement upon the owner, tenant and/or person having legal control of the premises upon which such
obstruction exists.
Such obstruction shall be removed within ten days from the date of receipt of such notice and order.
Any person receiving such notice and order may, within ten days from receipt thereof, request, in writing, a
hearing before the municipal court judge hearing housing code violations. The city traffic engineer shall notify
the person upon whom the notice and order have been served of the time and place of such hearing. If, after
such hearing, the municipal court judge finds that the obstruction in question does in fact constitute a public
nuisance, the judge shall order that such nuisance be abated within ten days from the date of such order.
Upon failure by any person to comply with such order of the judge, the traffic engineer shall cause the removal
of such obstruction by city forces and/or an independent contractor. The cost of such removal shall be billed to
the owner and/or person having legal control of the land. If unpaid for more than 30 days, such cost shall
become a lien against the property from which such obstruction is removed. The city clerk shall have authority
to file the lien on the public records of the county and to cancel the lien when paid.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Secs. 26-21—26-43. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - GENERAL PROHIBITION AND ABATEMENT PROCEDURES
Sec. 26-44. - Nuisances declared.
The following conditions may be declared to be a nuisance when any one of them endangers the health, welfare or good order
of the community:
Stagnant water on premises;
Any dead or decaying matter, weeds, vegetation, or any fruit, vegetable, animal or rodent, upon premises,
which is odorous or capable of causing disease or annoyance to the inhabitants of the city;
The generation of smoke or fumes in sufficient amounts to cause odor or annoyance to the inhabitants of the
city;
The pollution of public water or the injection of matter into the sewerage system which would be damaging
thereto;
Maintaining a dangerous or diseased animal or fowl;
Obstruction of a public street, highway or sidewalk without a permit;
Loud or unusual noises which are detrimental or annoying to the public, including without limiting the

foregoing, unusual loud disturbances in or around churches or multiple-family complexes such as loud music
and other activities in swimming pool and clubhouse areas;
Any business or building where illegal activities are habitually and commonly conducted in such manner as to
reasonable suggest that the owner or operator of the business or building was aware of the illegal activities
and failed to reasonably attempt to prevent such activities;
Any walls, trees, and buildings that may endanger persons or property;
Unused iceboxes, refrigerators and the like unless the doors, latches or locks thereof are removed;
All rubbish, litter, or debris, including, but not limited to, combustible and noncombustible waste materials,
garbage, wood, coal, coke, paper, rags, cartons, boxes, rubber, leather, tree branches, yard trimmings, tin cans,
metals, mineral matter, glass, crockery, and the residue from burning such items that may endanger the
health, welfare, good order, or beauty of the community;
It shall be unlawful to allow shrubbery or tree limbs on private property to protrude or hang so as to obstruct
the safe passage of pedestrians or motor vehicles. This subsection shall not apply to the removal of fallen
trees, dead trees, shrubbery, bushes, etc., on private property where such do not protrude into the
pedestrian/motor vehicle passageway;
Any other condition constituting a nuisance under state law.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-45. - Maintaining nuisance prohibited.
It is hereby declared to be an offense for any owner, agent, or tenant to maintain a nuisance. Each day a nuisance is
constituted shall constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-46. - Complaints.
Any official or inhabitant of the city may direct a complaint of a nuisance to the police department, which shall
investigate and may place the complaint on the municipal court docket for a hearing upon the basis of the
investigation. The municipal court, after five days' notice to the party involved, shall hold a hearing thereon, and
upon finding that a nuisance does exist shall issue an order to the owner, an agent in control of, or tenant in
possession, stating that a nuisance has been found to exist and that the nuisance must be abated within so many
hours or days as the judge shall deem reasonable, having consideration for the nature of the nuisance and its effect
on the public.
Animal control officers, building and license inspectors, health inspectors, public works inspectors, the fire
department officer, or other designees of the city may also receive complaints, investigate the same and place on
the court docket such complaints in the same manner as police officers.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-47. - Abatement—Generally.
In any case where the owner, agent or tenant fails to abate the nuisance in the time specified, or where the owner,
agent or tenant cannot be served with notice, or where the nature of the nuisance is such, in the opinion of the
judge, that it must be immediately abated, the judge may issue an order to the chief or police directing the nuisance
to be abated. The chief of police, in such case, shall keep a record of the expenses and cost of abating such
nuisance, and the costs shall be billed against the owner, agent or tenant for collection as for city revenues.
Other city departments shall assist the chief of police as is necessary in abating nuisances under this chapter.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
107/192
(1)
(2)
Sec. 26-48. - Same—Authority of mayor.
Nothing contained in this chapter shall prevent the mayor from summarily and without notice ordering the abatement of or
abating any nuisance that is a nuisance per se in the law or where the case is an urgent one and the health and safety of the public
or a portion thereof is in imminent danger.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)

ARTICLE IV. - WEEDS, DEBRIS AND INOPERABLE OR ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLES
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY
Sec. 26-70. - Denitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section,
except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
Building means any structure that encloses a space used for sheltering any occupancy.
Debris, for the purpose of this article, includes the residue from the burning of wood, coal, or other combustible material, as
well as paper, rags, cartons, boxes, wood, rubber, leather, fallen, broken or destroyed trees or tree limbs or other material or
objects not a part of the land and constituting a health or safety hazard.
Inoperable motor vehicles means any motor vehicles as defined in this section which is in a state of disrepair, wrecked,
dismantled, inoperative, abandoned or discarded. The term "inoperable motor vehicles" includes a motor vehicle that is incapable
of being moved under its own power.
Lot, for the purpose of this article, means one or any one or more of several contiguous parcels of land making up a block,
measured and set apart for use or occupancy.
Motor vehicle means any vehicle which is self-propelled and designated to travel along the ground and includes, but is not be
limited to, automobiles, buses, motorbikes, motorcycles, trucks, tractors, go-carts, golf carts, campers and trailers.
Weeds.
The term "weeds" means all objectionable growth, including weeds and grasses which serve as a breeding
place for mosquitoes and other unhealthy or undesirable insects, or as a refuge for snakes, rats or other
rodents, or that creates a fire or traffic hazard or provide a hiding place for persons.
The term "weeds" does not include flowers, shrubbery, trees and other growth used as a part of landscaping.
Wooded areas means those portions of lots consisting of a dense growth of trees, which exceed three inches in diameter.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Secs. 26-71—26-98. - Reserved.
DIVISION 2. - WEEDS AND DEBRIS
Subdivision I. - In General

Sec. 26-99. - Prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for the occupant of any lot of land or premises in the city, or the owner of any lot of land or
premises in the city, or any agent or representative of such owners or occupant, to permit or maintain on such lot
the growth thereon of objectionable weeds, the accumulation of debris, which distracts from the community
aesthetics, and endangers the public health, safety or welfare.
The following conditions shall constitute a nuisance as it relates to the growth of objectionable weeds:
Any lot on which a residential structure is built shall be deemed a nuisance if the growth of weeds as defined in
this article is 12 inches or more in height.
Any vacant lot located within a residential district or area shall be deemed a nuisance if the growth of weeds as
defined in this article exceeds 18 inches in height.
For the purpose of this section, wooded areas as defined in this article shall be exempt from the requirements of this
section.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-100. - Notice procedure.
When any objectionable condition as defined in this section is being permitted or maintained on any lot of land or
premises in the city in violation of section 26-99, the building inspector or chief of police, as applicable, or the
council's designee (the "official") shall notify in writing the occupant of such lot, or the owner thereof or their agents
or representatives, that the conditions existing upon their property constitute a nuisance, and setting forth the
actions to be taken to eliminate the objectionable conditions within 15 days, or within 30 days if the property is
zoned industrial or exceeds two acres in size. Failure of the owner or occupant to eliminate the conditions
constituting a nuisance within the allotted time period shall constitute an offense of this Code. An official may grant
a written extension upon a showing of reasonable cause, not to exceed an additional 15 days. Upon the expiration
of 15 days plus any extension, if any, the official shall issue a summons so changing the party notified and requiring
such party to appear in the municipal court for a hearing at a given time, place and date.
Notices shall be in writing and delivered in person or by certified mail to the occupant and/or owner or its agents or
representatives. If the official, following due diligence, is unable to serve such notice, the official shall cause such
notice to be published once a week for two consecutive weeks in the legal organ or general distribution of the court,
prior to taking any steps to abate said nuisance and prior to the running of the 15-day period for abatement of the
nuisance.
Any department, agency or individual charged with the enforcement of these regulations shall establish procedures
for the tracking, monitoring and the enforcement thereof consistent with these regulations.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Secs. 26-101—26-128. - Reserved.
Subdivision II. - Abatement
Sec. 26-129. - Authority.

In all cases where the owner, occupant or agent of a lot cannot be found, or if found and notified, neglects or refuses to abate
said nuisance within the time specified, it shall be lawful for the city to abate the same and remove the objectionable conditions
from the property. In such cases, the official shall notify the public works director who shall cause the nuisance to be abated and
the objectionable conditions to be removed from the property and shall assess the costs associated with said removal and charge
all costs thereof to the owner or representative. Said costs may constitute a lien against the property and be collected pursuant to
this Code; provided, however, that this shall not preclude other remedies available to the official for abating said nuisance or the

(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-130. - Procedure.
Complaint; contents; fine. When it becomes necessary to summons an owner or occupant of lands subject to the
provisions of this section, said summons shall be in the form of a written complaint setting forth, particularly, the
nature and location of the nuisance and the identity of the person complained against. If the court determined that
the conditions do in fact constitute a nuisance, the court shall issue an order specifying the time within which such
nuisance must be abated. In addition, the court may impose a fine not to exceed $500.00 for the offense of failure
to abate the nuisance within the period provided for in the section 26-100(a) if the court determines that the owner
or occupant unreasonably failed to abate the nuisance during that time period or prior to the court hearing.
Failure to comply; penalties. The failure of the owner or occupant to comply with the court's order to abate the
nuisance shall constitute an offense and shall subject the person to prosecution and penalties as provided in this
Code, including:
Community service to be performed with any private, nonprofit community service organization or any public
agency willing to participate and approved by municipal court. Violators shall not be used for any purpose
resulting in private gain to any person, except in accordance with state law. The role of the city in the
supervision of violators performing community service shall be a governmental function.
Any or all of these penalties within the discretion of the judge.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)

DIVISION 3. - ABANDONED OR INOPERABLE VEHICLES
Subdivision I. - In General
Sec. 26-159. - Prohibited.
It shall be unlawful to abandon any vehicle of any type within the city, nor shall any vehicle be left at any place within the city
for such time and under such circumstances as to cause the vehicle reasonably to appear to have been abandoned.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-160. - Unlawful to leave wrecked, nonoperating vehicle on street.
It shall be unlawful to leave any partially dismantled, nonoperating, wrecked or junked vehicle on any street, lane or highway
within the city.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
110/192
Sec. 26-161. - Keeping or storing nonoperating vehicles prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person in charge or control of any property within the city whether as owner, tenant, occupant,
lessee or agent thereof, to permit or allow any partially dismantled nonoperating, wrecked, junked or discarded vehicle an any kind
or character to remain on the property within the city longer than 15 days unless the vehicle is stored in an enclosed building or
located on the premises of a business enterprise operated in a lawful place or manner, when necessary to the operation of the
business enterprise.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Secs. 26-162—26-190. - Reserved.
Subdivision II. - Removal
Sec. 26-191. - Notice.
When any vehicle is thus abandoned, stored, parked or left on any vacant lot, property or premises within the city for a period
of more than 15 days, notice shall be served personally by the police department, or other authorized official designated by the
mayor, to the owner or person in charge of the property or premises if occupied, or if unoccupied by certified U.S. mail to the
owner or person in charge of the property or premises, with an additional notice posted on the vehicle to remove, store or dispose
of the vehicle within ten days from the date of the notice. The notice shall set forth the fact that the vehicle is abandoned, stored or
parked in violation of this division and that upon failure to remove, properly store, house or otherwise dispose of such vehicle, that
it will be removed, sold or disposed of by the city purchasing agent and that any proceeds arising from the sale thereof will be
applied first to payment of expenses incurred in connection with the removal and sale of the vehicles and any remaining balance
paid to the owner thereof.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-192. - Authority.
Upon violation of any provision of this division, the police department or other appropriate official designated by the mayor
shall be authorized to have any vehicle thus abandoned on the streets or lanes of the city removed, impounded and stored
immediately pending the sale or other disposition thereof as provided in this article.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-193. - Advertisement; sale of impounded vehicle.
Upon failure of the owner to claim the vehicle within 30 days after it has been impounded by the police department or other
authorized official, it shall be advertised and sold by the city clerk. The advertisement shall be published on three consecutive
weeks in the official newspaper of the city wherein all legal advertisements are published and shall describe and identify the
vehicle to be sold, the fact that it has been impounded by the police department as an abandoned vehicle and will be sold at the
place where stored to the highest bidder for cash on a date certain ten days after the publication of the last notice unless the
vehicle shall have been claimed by the owner and all costs incurred in connection with the removal, storage and advertisement
thereof are paid prior thereto.
(Ord. of 11-14-2005)
Sec. 26-194. - Posting notice on removed vehicle; redemption by owner.

Chapter 28 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 28-1. - Disobeying police ocer.
It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully fail or refuse to comply with any lawful order or direction of a police officer of the
city.
(Code 1973, § 10-5)
Sec. 28-2. - Curfew for underage persons.
For the purpose of this section, the following definition shall apply:
Public place means:
Any street, highway, alley, or right-of-way, to include sidewalks, any park, playground, mall, or other place or
building open to the public;
Any cemetery, school yard, body of water or watercourse;
Any privately or publicly owned place of amusement, entertainment or public accommodation including
parking lots, and other areas adjacent thereto; and
Any vacant lot or land.
It shall be unlawful for any minor between four years of age and 18 years of age to loiter, wander, stroll, or play in or
upon the public streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds or other public grounds, public places, public
buildings, places of amusement, eating places, vacant lots, or any place unsupervised by an adult 21 years of age or
older having the lawful authority to be at such places between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 2:30 p.m. on any school
day; provided, however, that the provision of this section shall not apply in the following incidents:
When a minor is accompanied by his parent, guardian, or other adult person 21 years of age or older having
the lawful care and custody of the minor;
When the minor is upon an emergency errand directed by his parent, guardian, or other adult person 21 years
of age or older having the lawful care and custody of the minor;
When the minor is returning directly home from lawful employment that makes it necessary to be in the places
referenced in this subsection during the prescribed period of time;
When the minor is in a motor vehicle with parental consent for normal travel with interstate and intrastate
travel through the city being excepted in all cases from this section;
When the minor is enrolled in a valid home study program as authorized by O.C.G.A. § 20-2-690;
When the minor has completed all course study requirements for high school graduation;
When the minor is married in accordance with applicable law;

When the minor has written proof from school authorities that he is excused from school attendance at that
particular time; or
When the minor is participating in an approved school or study activity, which requires the minor to be off
school property.
No parent or legal guardian of a minor between four years of age and 18 years of age shall negligently allow a minor
to violate subsection (b) of this section.
Upon the conviction of negligently allowing a minor to violate subsection (b) of this section, a person shall be guilty
of a misdemeanor and be punished in accordance with the city Charter. Each citation of this section shall constitute
a separate offense. It shall be an affirmative defense if the parent or legal guardian has initiated the jurisdiction of
the juvenile court against the minor prior to the time that the minor was found in violation of subsection (b) of this
section. Any minor who violates subsection (b) of this section is subject to the jurisdiction of the juvenile court.
A police officer shall transport any minor found in violation of subsection (b) of this section to a designated school
district facility. A minor transported to the school district facility will be released to the custody of the school officials
or to the custody of his parent or legal guardian.
If a minor is suspended or expelled from school, that minor's parent or legal guardian, for the duration of the
suspension or expulsion, shall:
Personally supervise the minor or arrange for a responsible adult 21 years of age or older to supervise the
minor required to be in attendance at school had he not been expelled or suspended; and
Prohibit the minor from being in any public place at the times the minor would have been required to be in
attendance at school had he not been suspended or expelled unless:
The minor is accompanied by his parent or legal guardian or responsible adult, 21 years of age or older,
selected by the parent or legal guardian to supervise the minor; or
The minor is employed pursuant to an age or schooling certificate during the actual working hours or
traveling directly to or from the job site.
Upon conviction of a violation of subsection (b) of this section, a person shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
Any minor who violates subsection (b) of this section is subject to the jurisdiction of the juvenile court.
It shall be an affirmative defense if the parent or legal guardian has initiated the jurisdiction of the juvenile court
against the minor prior to the time that he violated subsection (b) of this section.
(Ord. of 12-9-2002, §§ 1—9)
Secs. 28-3—28-22. - Reserved.
ARTICLE II. - OFFENSES INVOLVING PROPERTY RIGHTS
Sec. 28-23. - Billposting without permission or on utility poles.
It shall be unlawful for anyone to put any bill or placard upon any wall, fence, building, post or other property of another
without permission of the owner. It shall be unlawful for any person to put any bill or placard on any telephone pole or electric
light pole in the city.
(Code 1973, § 10-11)
Secs. 28-24—28-49. - Reserved.
ARTICLE III. - OFFENSES INVOLVING PUBLIC SAFETY

Sec. 28-50. - Discharging rearms; exceptions.
It shall be unlawful for any person to shoot firearms in the city. This section does not apply to:
Persons exercising their legal right of self-defense or defense or others.
Members or the Armed Forces of the United States or the National Guard while engaged in official duties as
such.
Law enforcement officers engaged in official duties as such.
Persons authorized by the council.
(Code 1973, § 10-9)
State law reference— Local firearms ordinances, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-173.
Sec. 28-51. - Fireworks.
It shall be unlawful for any person to set off, light, explode, or shoot any firecracker, Roman candle, sparkler, or pyrotechnic of
any type whatsoever, within the city except upon written permission of the council which may permit their use as public
entertainment by licensed bonded festival operators.
(Code 1973, § 10-7)
State law reference— Fireworks, O.C.G.A. § 25-10-1 et seq.
Sec. 28-52. - Explosives.
Explosives may be used in the city for construction and demolition purposes only by qualified personnel and then only upon
written consent of the council.
(Code 1973, § 10-8)
State law reference— Blasting, O.C.G.A. § 25-8-1 et seq.
Sec. 28-53. - Slings.
No person shall possess or use any Alabama or rubber sling.
(Code 1973, § 10-2(25))
Sec. 28-54. - Ball playing in streets.
It shall be unlawful for any person to play ball by throwing, tossing or catching the same for amusement of pastime, or
otherwise, on the streets of the city.
(Code 1973, § 10-10)
Secs. 28-55—28-81. - Reserved.
ARTICLE IV. - OFFENSES INVOLVING PUBLIC PEACE AND ORDER
Sec. 28-82. - Disorderly conduct.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
114/192
(a)
(b)
(1)
No person shall engage in any disorderly conduct in the city.
(Code 1973, § 10-2(3))
State law reference— Local disorderly conduct ordinances authorized, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-39.
Sec. 28-83. - Disorderly meetings or assemblages.
No person shall conduct or engage or participate in any disorderly meetings or assemblages.
(Code 1973, § 10-2(15))
State law reference— Unlawful assembly, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-33.
Sec. 28-84. - Keeping disorderly houses.
Any person who shall permit parties of disorderly character or acting in any disorderly manner to assemble upon his premises,
either owned or occupied by him, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
(Code 1973, § 10-2(37))
State law reference— Maintaining a disorderly house, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-44.
Sec. 28-85. - Public intoxication.
A person who shall be and appear in an intoxicated condition in any public place or within the curtilage of any private
residence not his own other than by invitation of the owner or lawful occupant, which condition is made manifest by
boisterousness, by indecent condition or act, or by vulgar, profane, loud, or unbecoming language, is guilty of a misdemeanor.
(Code 1973, § 10-2(21))
State law reference— Public intoxication, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41.
Sec. 28-86. - Disturbing the peace.
No person shall engage in any conduct that manifestly tends to the disturbance of the public peace or the annoyance of the
citizens.
(Code 1973, § 10-2(31))
Sec. 28-87. - Unreasonably loud, disturbing and unnecessary noise.
General prohibition. The creating of any unreasonable loud, disturbing and unnecessary noise within the limits of
the city is prohibited. Noise of such character, intensity or duration as to be detrimental to the life or health of any
individual, or in disturbance of the public peace and welfare is prohibited. In addition, at any time between the
hours of 9:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. Sunday through Thursday and 11:00 p.m. Friday and Saturday and 9:00 a.m.
Saturday and Sunday, it shall be deemed a violation of this section if any noise regulated or prohibited under the
provisions of this section is readily audible in another home, residence, apartment or building in which the usual
openings such as windows and doors are closed. The person causing the noise, or the owner, lessee or other person
in control of the property from which the noise is emanating shall be deemed to be in violation of this section.
Certain acts declared offensive. The following acts, among others, are declared to be loud, disturbing and
unnecessary noises and noises in violation of this section, but this enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive,
namely:
Horns. The sounding of any horn or signal device on any automobile, motorcycle, bus, or other vehicle, while

not in motion except as a danger signal if another vehicle is approaching apparently out of control, or, if in
motion, only as a danger signal; the creation by means of any such signal device for any unreasonably loud or
harsh sound or the sounding of such device for an unnecessary or unreasonable period of time;
Musical instruments. The playing of any radio, phonograph or any musical instrument in such a manner or
with such volume, as to annoy or disturb the quiet comfort or repose of persons in any office, hospital or in
any dwelling, hotel or other type of residence, or any persons in the vicinity, except this section shall not apply
to schools of music between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m.;
Voices. Yelling, shouting, hooting, whistling or singing at any time or place so as to annoy or disturb quiet,
comfort or repose of persons in any hospital, dwelling, hotel or other type of residence, or any persons in the
vicinity. The provisions of this section shall apply to voices or other noise originating within a building or
residence and to noise produced by animals such as dogs, cats or others, whether housed in a building or an
open enclosure, and if the noise continues steadily or intermittently during a period in excess of ten minutes in
anyone day or night. In the case of animals, the owner or person in immediate control of the property on
which the animal is housed shall be deemed responsible. In the case of noise emanating from a residence or
apartment, the owner, lessee, renter or other person deemed to be in immediate control of the home,
apartment or building shall be deemed responsible. It shall be deemed a violation if the noise, caused by
persons or animals is readily audible in any nearby home, apartment, building or other structure when its
natural opening such as doors and windows are closed;
Noisy vehicles. The use of any automobile, motorcycle, or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded or in such manner
as to create loud and unnecessary granting, grinding, or rattling, or other noise;
Steam whistles. The blowing of any steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler, except to give notice of the
time to begin or stop work, or as a warning of fire or danger, or upon request of proper city authority;
Exhausts. To discharge into the open air the exhaust of any stationary steam engine, stationary internal
combustion engine, motor vehicle or motorboat engine, except though a muffler or other device which will
effectively prevent loud or explosive noises therefrom;
Construction work. The erection, including excavation, demolition, alteration or repair of any building in any
residential district or section, or the excavation of streets and highways in any residential district or section,
other than between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. on weekdays, except in the cases of urgent necessity
and then only with a permit from the city engineer, building inspector, chief of police or designee of the
council, which permit may be granted for a period not to exceed 60 days while the emergency continues. If the
city engineer, building inspector, or chief of police or designee of the council, or the director of inspections and
fees should determine that the public health and safety will not be impaired by the erection, demolition,
alteration or repair of any building, or the excavation of streets and highways within the hours of 10:00 p.m.
and 7:00 a.m., and if he shall further determine that loss or inconvenience would result to any party in interest,
the city engineer or the director of inspections and fees may grant permission for such work to be done within
the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m., upon application being made at the time the permit for work is awarded
or during the progress of the work;
Noises near schools, hospitals, churches, etc. The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any
school, institution of learning, church or court while they are in session, or adjacent to any hospital, which
unreasonably interferes with the workings or sessions thereof;
Loudspeakers on vehicles. The use of mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks or other moving or
standing vehicles for advertising or other purposes; and
Garbage dumpsters. The loading, unloading, opening, closing, lifting or otherwise handling of dumpsters or
other garbage containers between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. when the sound therefrom disturbs
the quiet comfort or repose of persons on any house, apartment, hotel or other type of property used for

Exceptions. None of the foregoing terms or prohibitions shall apply to or be enforced against:

ARTICLE V. - OFFENSES INVOLVING PUBLIC MORALS
Sec. 28-120. - Public drinking.
It shall be unlawful for any person to drink spirituous or malt beverages, or intoxicating liquors upon any street, alley,
sidewalk, or public property within the city. This section shall not apply to conduct prohibited by O.C.G.A. § 40-6-253 or prohibit
conduct exempted from such section.
(Code 1973, § 10-12)

Sec. 28-131. - Denitions and prohibitions.
A person commits the offense of public indecency when he or she performs any of the following acts in a place where a person
should reasonably expect to be in view of the public:
An actual or simulated act of sexual intercourse or masturbation;
Exposure of the genitals;
A lewd appearance in a state of partial or complete nudity;
A lewd caress or indecent fondling of the body of another person;
A lewd caress or indecent fondling of the sexual organs of any person, including oneself;
Urination or defecation; or
Appears wearing pants or skirts more than three inches below the top of the hips (crest of the ilium) exposing
the skin or undergarments.
(Res. of 12-19-2011, § 1)
Sec. 28-132. - Enforcement.
The City of Edison Police Department shall be the enforcement authority for this article. The mayor and council may
also authorize other departments as may be deemed necessary to support enforcement.
Any violation of this article may also be enforced by a citation or accusation returnable to the recorder's court or by
any other legal means as set forth in this Code.
A violation of this article shall be punishable as a misdemeanor.
A fine of not less than $25.00 on the first offense and not more than $200.00 for each subsequent offense may be
imposed. In addition to or in lieu of a fine, the court may order such person to participate in up to 40 hours of court
approved community service activities.
(Res. of 12-19-2011, § 1)
Sec. 28-133. - Defenses.
It is a defense under this article if it is determined, after a hearing or trial, that the person was exercising rights protected by
the federal or state constitution. Any defense under this article must be asserted prior to any hearing or trial in the matter.
(Res. of 12-19-2011, § 1)

State Law reference— Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq.; litter control, O.C.G.A. §

Sec. 30-19. - Denitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section,
except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
Agent means any person who receives the rent in whole or in part from another party for that person's use of any premises.
Commercial wastes means all water products from manufacturing or commercial establishments, cinders, and ashes from
commercial boilers, cardboard and wooden boxes, crates and barrels.
Garbage means domestic wastes composed of meat, vegetable and fruit scraps, cans, bottles, paper, cardboard, rags, ashes
and other such waste matter normally to be disposed of from residences, churches, schools, small business establishments and
similar places.
Occupant means any person living or doing business on any premises, or any premises where construction of any kind is in
progress and where employees or workmen are engaged in their regular employment. The term "occupant" includes the
contractor, foreman or other person in charge over such workmen. The term "occupant" also includes the person in charge of any
market or stall in any market.
Premises means land, buildings or other structures, vehicles, or parts thereof, upon or in which refuse is stored.
Trash includes yard wastes, such as, weeds, grass and hedge trimmings, leaves, brush, tree limbs and similar items.
(Code 1973, § 8-1)
Sec. 30-20. - Place for disposal.
Every person who disposes of any garbage, trash or commercial wastes, whether required to do so by this article or otherwise,
shall make such disposal at a place designated by the city.
(Code 1973, § 8-2)
Sec. 30-21. - Garbage container standards.
All containers used for the temporary storage of garbage by occupants shall:
Be of metal or plastic;
Be of less than 41-gallon capacity;
Have adequate handles for the handling of the lid as well as container; and
Be used only so long as it is maintained in a watertight condition in its usual location and orientation.
(Code 1973, § 8-3)
Sec. 30-22. - Containers meeting proper standards required.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances
119/192
(1)
(2)
No garbage shall be stored or placed outside for pickup by collectors except in containers meeting the standards established
in section 30-21.
(Code 1973, § 8-4)
Sec. 30-23. - Disturbing container contents prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to pick from or disturb the contents of any garbage container or vessel or other containers
provided for in this article.
(Code 1973, § 8-5)
Sec. 30-24. - Containers to be covered.
Garbage containers shall be tightly covered at all times except when momentarily opened to receive the garbage or to have
the contents therefrom removed.
(Code 1973, § 8-6)
Sec. 30-25. - Removing container cover prohibited except when done by authorized person.
When a garbage container is placed outside of any premises, it shall be unlawful and a violation of this Code for any person
engaged in the removal of garbage or for any other person to remove the cover from such garbage container except for the
purpose of emptying its contents into a duly authorized garbage collector. It shall also be a violation of this Code to throw such
garbage container on the street or sidewalk, and all persons engaged in the removal of garbage shall after emptying said container
replace said cover tightly on said container.
(Code 1973, § 8-7)
Sec. 30-26. - Littering streets or lots with carcasses, vegetables, etc., prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, place or allow to remain on any street, alley, or on the lot of another any
discarded flesh or vegetable, fruit or dead carcass or other offensive matter calculated to annoy the citizens of the neighborhood,
or endanger their health.
(Code 1973, § 8-10)

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
Sec. 32-1. - Duties and responsibilities of mayor.
The mayor, or a person designated by the mayor, shall:
Supervise the streets, roads, alleys, lanes and highways of the city;
Keep the streets, roads, alleys, lanes and highways in good repair;

Supervise all street work and direct the same;
Have control of and provide for shade trees, tree boxes, and bridges; and
Have cognizance of all matters related thereto.
(Code 1973, § 13-2)
Sec. 32-2. - Throwing rubbish, trash, etc., on streets or sidewalks prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or cause to be thrown in or upon any of the streets, sidewalks, or public property,
or upon any private property, without the consent of the owner, any rubbish, waste material, tin cans, refuse, trash, garbage, or
litter of any kind or description
(Code 1973, § 13-7; Ord. of 8-12-1986)
State law reference— Litter control, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-42 et seq.; unlawful dumping, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-51 et seq.
Sec. 32-3. - Building materials.
Permitted on thoroughfares when necessary; night lighting. It shall be unlawful for any mechanic or builder, in the
exercise of his trade in the city, to place his lumber or material in such a position as to obstruct the streets,
sidewalks or public squares with such material, except when it becomes necessary for building purposes, and then
only so much as is absolutely required at such place. During the time the streets, sidewalks, or public squares are
obstructed, the owners or builders shall cause a lamp or lantern, with good light, from dark until daylight to be hung
on both sides of such obstruction.
Removal as soon as practicable. All mechanics or builders who may place any lumber or other building material on
the streets, sidewalks or public squares, shall remove the same, with all rubbish or trash which may accumulate in
consequence thereof, as soon as practicable, and in no case shall they be allowed to leave such material or rubbish
thereon for longer than 48 hours after the completion of the work upon which they may be engaged.
Liability of owner. Any owner of property, where mechanics or builders are engaged at work, who shall allow such
lumber, material or rubbish as is prohibited in subsections (a) and (b) of this section to remain upon the street,
sidewalk or public square, shall be punished in the same manner as the mechanic himself.
(Code 1973, §§ 13-8—13-10)
Sec. 32-4. - Removing sand, gravel, etc., from public roadways prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to dig or scrape up or carry away sand, gravel, dirt, rock or earth from any public way in the
city.
(Code 1973, § 13-13)
Sec. 32-5. - Driveway, curb cut installation.
Permit required; fee. No curb cuts shall be made, and no driveway culverts shall be installed, until a permit in
writing is obtained from the city council and payment is made to the city treasurer of monies in the amount
estimated by the council as being necessary to finance the costs of repairs to the streets, curbs, drainageways, or
sidewalks.
City clerk's duty. It shall be the responsibility of the city clerk, upon the issuance of the permit to install said
driveways or curb cuts, to issue a work order to appropriate city personnel for the attendant repairs to city property.
(Code 1973, § 13-14)
Sec. 32-6. - Obstructing drains prohibited.
5/9/2019 Edison, GA Code of Ordinances

It shall be unlawful for any person to throw any trash or other thing whatever into, or obstruct in any way whatever, any ditch,
gutter or drain, or in any way impede or prevent the free flow of water through such drain, ditch or gutter.
(Code 1973, § 9-3)
Sec. 32-7. - Street numbering system.
Owner responsible for costs. The numbering of stores, residences and buildings shall be done at the cost and
expense of the owners.
City council to supervise installation. The installation of the system of street numbering is to be under the
supervision of the city council.
(Code 1973, § 13-1)
Sec. 32-8. - Obstructing streets.
Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for anyone to obstruct any street, lane, alley, sidewalk or public square by any porch
steps, fence or other obstruction or nuisance whatever.
Removal; penalty. The city shall have all such obstructions or nuisances removed by serving written notice upon the
owner or occupant of the premises, and the party so obstructing, and upon failure to comply with such notice, after
24 hours, the parties shall be punished as prescribed in general penalty section 1-7, and the city council shall have
the same removed at the expense of such owner, occupant or party obstructing, and an execution shall issue
therefor.
(Code 1973, § 13-3)
Sec. 32-9. - Obstructing intersections.
Prohibited; exception. No structure, wall, fence, sign, shrubbery, or trees shall be erected, planted or maintained on
any lot which will obstruct the view of a driver of a vehicle approaching an intersection, excepting that shade trees
will be permitted when all branches are not less than eight feet above the street level.
Corner lots. In the case of corner lots, subsection (a) of this section means there shall be provided an unobstructed
triangular area formed by the street property lines and a line connecting them at points 25 feet from the
intersection of said street lines or, in cases of a rounded corner, from the intersection of the street property lines
extended.
(Code 1973, § 13-4)
Sec. 32-10. - Allowing animals and vehicles to cause inconvenience prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to hitch or fasten any horse, mule or other animal to any tree, fence, house or paling along
the city streets or on a public square, or to allow his horses or mules to run at large on the public streets or squares, or to drive any
truck, cart, or other vehicle, or ride any horse or other animal upon the sidewalks, to the inconvenience of persons passing (except
in the case of trucks and for the purpose of loading and unloading), or permit the same to obstruct the sidewalks.
(Code 1973, § 13-4)
Sec. 32-11. - Assembling for purpose of vending or showing wares prohibited when obstruction created.
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct any street, sidewalk or public square for the purpose of selling, vending, or
showing wares or merchandise, nor persons assembled for any purpose to obstruct the same.
(Code 1973, § 13-6)

(2)
Sec. 32-12. - Closing street by private person prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to close up any public street or alley by a fence or other obstruction.
(Code 1973, § 13-12)
